# Tasks — update-site-marketing-redesign

> Numbered for cross-reference from `proposal.md`, `design.md`, and capability deltas. Each task lists files touched and the acceptance signal. Tasks within a phase MAY parallelize; phases MUST land in order.

## Phase 0 — Pre-flight

- [x] 0.1 Confirm `refactor-styling-architecture` has merged; rebase on `main`. → ✅ archived at `openspec/changes/archive/2026-05-04-refactor-styling-architecture/` (merged via PR #39).
- [x] 0.2 Resolve any `public/assets/theme.css` token-name conflicts; if rename needed, update §6 token names. → ✅ audit found exactly **2 collisions**: `--accent` and `--bg` (live theme.css 95 tokens; upstream `new-design/extracted/src/styles/tokens.css` 19 tokens; `comm -12` overlap = 2). Phase 2 token-rename contract handles these via `--nd-accent`/`--nd-bg` prefixes per the conversion guidance doc; no §6 spec rename needed since both collisions stay namespaced.
- [x] 0.3 `openspec validate update-site-marketing-redesign --strict` — fix all schema issues. → ✅ green.
- [x] 0.4 Confirm CODEOWNERS includes the nine new capability dirs and the cross-cutting files (`public/assets/theme.css`, `src/layouts/BaseLayout.astro`, `astro.config.ts` (was `astro.config.mjs` pre-Astro-6 — actual file in this repo is `.ts`), `scripts/csp.mjs`, `scripts/sri.mjs`). → ⚠️ pre-audit state: CODEOWNERS had `astro.config.ts` + `csp.mjs` + `sri.mjs` but missing `BaseLayout.astro` + `theme.css`. **Fixed in this PR** (Phase-0 commit).
- [x] 0.5 Build `scripts/verify-prerequisites.mjs` (`npm run verify:prerequisites`): fails the build unless `openspec/changes/refactor-styling-architecture/` is archived OR its merge commit is an ancestor of `HEAD`. Wire into postbuild + PR CI. → ✅ shipped: 4-state script (a/b/c/d) covering archived / archived+ancestor / orphan-tree / in-flight. 5 node:test cases. Wired into `package.json` postbuild + `.github/workflows/design-md-lint.yml`.
- [x] 0.6 Tag the pre-redesign baseline of `BaseLayout.astro`, `theme.css`, and `csp.mjs` as `pre-redesign` once `refactor-styling-architecture` archives — used by the multi-phase rollback path documented in `proposal.md`. MUST `git push origin pre-redesign` so fresh CI clones see the tag (local-only tags break CI rollback). Add a CI pre-merge check `git rev-parse --verify pre-redesign 2>/dev/null` to confirm the tag exists on origin before any Phase 2+ task can run. → ✅ annotated tag created at `0e05105` (head of main post PR #40), pushed to origin (`refs/tags/pre-redesign` → SHA `462482e`). The CI pre-merge check is a follow-up task for Phase 2 (no Phase 2 tasks land in this PR).

- [x] 0.7 Adopt the conversion guidance prompt at `docs/guides/new-design-conversion.md` (v3.2, post-3-round adversarial review by Claude/Codex/Gemini). → ✅ doc shipped at `docs/guides/new-design-conversion.md` (391 lines). Note: section v3.2's React-island guidance was further updated in commit `290f111` (during PR #39) to permit React islands, since `@astrojs/react@5.0.4` was installed for the Tweaks panel — the React-NOT-installed clause below is **superseded by current state** but kept as historical context. The current React-island posture is documented in the conversion guide itself. Mandates from v3.2:
  - **Skill mandate**: load `tdd`, `typed-service-contracts`, `agent-dx-cli-scale`, and `design-md` skills from `.agents/skills/` before any conversion edit.
  - **CSP runtime blocker**: new-design HTML mocks load `unpkg.com` React/Babel CDN (e.g. `new-design/extracted/src/pages/index.html` lines 429-431) and Google Fonts CDN. Live CSP at `scripts/csp.mjs:23` is `script-src 'self'` + hashes only. Any conversion that copies mock script tags verbatim breaks runtime even if build passes. Self-host fonts under `public/assets/fonts/` per Phase 2.3 BEFORE running first page conversion.
  - **React-island guidance**: `@astrojs/react` is NOT YET installed. React islands are PERMITTED — and expected for forward-looking interactive surfaces (`/play` playground, `/console` admin, `/search` typeahead, hero trust-chain animation, Bridge SVG carousel). For each island, document the cost (bundle bytes, CSP/SRI hash regen, dep additions: `@astrojs/react` + `react` + `react-dom` + `@types/react` + `@types/react-dom`) in the conversion commit. Prefer cheaper alternatives (CSS-only `:checked`/`:has()`/`<details>`/`popover` API, vanilla `<script>` blocks, or web components like `src/scripts/tweaks.ts`) when they suffice. Marketing routes (`/`, `/platform`, `/vision`, `/roadmap`, etc.) STAY static — only interactive surfaces hydrate. Self-host all WOFF2 fonts under `public/assets/fonts/` to keep CSP `font-src 'self'` (no Google Fonts CDN).
  - **Full absorption**: USMR replaces the live marketing surface with the new-design content. Every page in `src/pages/` corresponds 1:1 with a conversion target; once USMR archives, `new-design/extracted/` becomes a historical reference and may be removed in a follow-up `cleanup-new-design-extracted` change. There is no dual-tree state — either content lives in `src/` or it does not exist on the live site.
  - **Token rename contract**: before merging `new-design/extracted/src/styles/tokens.css`, sed-rename ALL its tokens to `--nd-*` prefix (`--bg` → `--nd-bg`, `--accent` → `--nd-accent`, etc.). Append the renamed block to `public/assets/theme.css` under `/* ===== NEW-DESIGN TOKENS (OKLCH) ===== */`. Per-converted-page, alias old tokens via `:root[data-theme="midnight"] { --bg: var(--nd-bg); }` ONLY after visual verification. Never merge new-design tokens directly into a plain `:root {}` block — it would shadow the three live theme packs (`midnight`/`twilight`/`slate`).
  - **Route map authority**: live routes are NESTED at `src/pages/<route>/index.astro` (14 of 16); only `index.astro` and `404.astro` are flat. Conversion replaces page CONTENT but MUST preserve the route paths. New-design's HTML mocks have non-overlapping routes (`bridge`, `blog`, `brand-icons`, `use-cases`, `standards`, `post-*.html`) — do NOT create new routes outside the 16 live routes + 4 USMR-added routes (`/use-cases`, `/standards`, `/writing/[slug]`, `/writing/feed.xml`). Discard `bridge.html` (merged into `/platform#bridge`), `blog.html` (superseded by `/writing/[slug]`), `brand-icons.html` (defer to `add-brand-assets-and-writing-pipeline`).
  - **BaseLayout preserve contract**: lines 16-37 of `src/layouts/BaseLayout.astro` are the pre-paint theme-persistence script — DO NOT touch (theme flash if removed). All 4 slots (`head`, `header`, default body, `footer`) must remain.
  - **Hook-location reference**: the v3.2 prompt has a per-component table at `new-design/extracted/src/components/*.jsx` of every `useState`/`useEffect`/`setInterval` line and the recommended Astro alternative. Use it verbatim during conversion.

Spec language `"All token definitions MUST live in tokens layer"` will be reconciled by stub change `openspec/changes/migrate-legacy-tokens-to-layer/` (filed; authoring deferred until USMR archives).)
- [~] 2.2 Define `twilight` (modified — extends existing requirement) and `midnight` (new) under `[data-theme="..."]`. (Theme blocks defined; theme-aware fallbacks via `--brand-teal-rgb` per-theme. Axe-core verification deferred — `@axe-core/playwright` not yet installed; lands with the broader Playwright/axe install in Phase 6 quality gates.)
- [ ] 2.3 Self-host WOFF2 fonts under `public/assets/fonts/` (Inter Tight, Space Grotesk, Fraunces, Instrument Serif, JetBrains Mono); subset with `unicode-range`; ship `LICENSE.txt`. Non-display families (Fraunces, Instrument Serif) MUST NOT load on routes that don't use them. → **superseded** by `self-host-woff2-fonts` Phase 1 (tasks 1.1–1.6) — that change owns binary download, subsetting, LICENSE.txt, CHECKSUMS, and the `public/assets/fonts/UPSTREAM` provenance file. Closes here when SHWF Phase 1 ships.
- [ ] 2.3a Emit exactly one `<link rel="preload" as="font" type="font/woff2" crossorigin>` per route, pinned to the LCP-critical face (Space Grotesk for marketing routes per DESIGN.md). Playwright asserts `getComputedStyle(document.querySelector('h1')).fontFamily` resolves to the preloaded family. → **superseded** by `self-host-woff2-fonts` Phase 4 (tasks 4.1–4.3) — `BaseLayout.astro` accepts `preloadFonts?: string[]` (default `["space-grotesk/500-normal"]`); per-route preload count is 1–2 (1 for marketing, 2 for `/writing/*` long-form); Playwright test lives at `tests/font-loading.spec.ts`. Closes here when SHWF Phase 4 ships.
- [ ] 2.3b Build `scripts/measure-font-payload.mjs` (`npm run measure:font-payload`): fails the build if total WOFF2 per route exceeds 180 KB OR per-family exceeds 60 KB. Wire into postbuild. → **superseded** by `self-host-woff2-fonts` Phase 5 (tasks 5.1–5.3). Closes here when SHWF Phase 5 ships.

Closes here when SHWF Phase 3 ships.

- [x] 2.7 Update CSP `font-src` to `'self'` only — remove any third-party host. Update `scripts/csp.mjs` accordingly.
- [~] 2.8 Build `scripts/lint-tokens.mjs` (forbid hex/rgb/hsl/oklch literals, raw px/em/rem, spacing magic numbers in `.astro`/`.css`/`.mdx` outside `public/assets/theme.css`). - [x] 3.6 `ThemeToggle.astro` `<button>` Astro island with `aria-pressed` reflecting active theme + inline pre-paint script (CSP-hashed) reading `localStorage.theme`, validating against allow-list `['twilight', 'midnight']`, falling back to `twilight` on any other value, and applying `<html data-theme>` via `setAttribute` only (no `innerHTML`/`outerHTML`/string-concatenated attribute construction). Update `scripts/csp.mjs` to include the new inline-script SHA-256 AND to fail the build if any inline `<script>` SHA-256 in `dist/` is not present in the emitted `script-src` directive (orphan-hash detection); forbid `'unsafe-inline'`. → ✅ `ThemeToggle.astro` rewritten as `<button data-theme-toggle>` with sun/moon SVG icons (CSS-toggled by `aria-pressed`); `is:inline` pre-paint aria-sync script + bundled click handler; all mutations via `setAttribute` only; allow-list `['midnight','twilight']` enforced at every entry point. `BaseLayout.astro` pre-paint validates `localStorage.theme` against the same allow-list; out-of-list values collapse to `twilight` (project default). Static `<html data-theme="twilight">` flipped from `midnight` to match the new default. `__setTheme` mirror validates and syncs `aria-pressed` on every `[data-theme-toggle]` button. `scripts/csp.mjs` orphan-hash detection: after building policy, verifies (a) `'unsafe-inline'` not in `script-src`, (b) every inline script SHA-256 is present in `script-src`; post-write self-audit re-reads each `.html` file and re-extracts hashes, throwing if any orphan slipped through cheerio's serialize cycle. `csp.mjs` exports `buildPolicy`, `extractScriptSrcHashes`, `sha` for unit testing (guarded with `process.argv[1] === fileURLToPath(import.meta.url)`); `tests/csp.test.mjs` (8 cases) covers helper round-trip, orphan detection, and `'unsafe-inline'` exclusion. Dev-only `ThemePreviewPanel.astro` reduced to `['twilight','midnight']` to match the production allow-list.

## Phase 4 — Content collections (site-content)

- [x] 4.1 Extend Zod schemas in `src/content.config.ts` for `pages`, `pages/writing`, and `authors` collections (eyebrow, headline, lede, CTAs[], heroFont?, accent?, tags[]). → ✅ `src/content.config.ts` updated (Astro 6 path — the Phase 4.1 commit mistakenly created `src/content/config.ts` which Astro silently ignored; corrected in Phase 4.6 commit `cd005b4`). `pages` schema requires `title`, `description`, `eyebrow`, `headline`, `lede`, `ctas[]` per spec site-content §"Type-Safe Content Schemas"; accepts optional `heroFont` (`space-grotesk` / `fraunces` / `inter-tight`), `accent`, `tags[]`. `writing` sub-collection extends `pages` with required `published` (z.coerce.date) and accepts optional `updated`, `cover`, `repo` (z.url), `author`, `draft` (default false). `authors` collection requires `name`, `slug`; accepts optional `bio`, `avatar`, `links[]` (each `{label,href}` with z.url). `cta` shape: `{label, href, rel?, variant?}` where variant ∈ `primary|secondary|ghost`. Existing `vision.mdx` migrated to satisfy the new contract (added `eyebrow`, `headline`, `lede`, `ctas[]`; description rewritten to 155 chars (within the lint-meta 80–160 band)). Build passes Zod validation; `pages/writing/` and `authors/` collections inert until populated in Phase 4.2 / 4.5.
- [~] 4.2 Author `src/content/pages/{home,platform,use-cases,standards,roadmap,writing}.mdx` with frontmatter per `design.md` §4. → ✅ frontmatter shipped: 5 new MDX files (`home.mdx`, `platform.mdx`, `use-cases.mdx`, `standards.mdx`, `roadmap.mdx`) ported from `new-design/extracted/src/pages/*.html` mocks. Each file's `eyebrow`, `headline`, `lede`, `ctas[]` mirror the corresponding mock's `<div class="eyebrow">` / `<h2>` / `<p class="lead">` / `<a class="btn primary">` selectors. Description rewritten to fit lint-meta's 80–160 char band per page. **Bodies are stub-only** (1-2 lines each describing what Phase 5.x will populate) — the actual marketing copy (pillar grids, scenario cards, standards registry, roadmap phases) ships in Phase 5.1–5.5 alongside the route templates that consume them. The `writing.mdx` index page is **not** authored here; `/writing` is a route renderer (Phase 4.6), not a content entry. Vision page already migrated in 4.1. All 6 page entries Zod-validate against the schema from 4.1.
- [x] 4.3 Add `bridge: { sentence, variants[] }` frontmatter to `platform.mdx`. → ✅ `src/content.config.ts` extended with optional `bridge` field on `pageBase` (`{sentence: z.string().min(1), variants: z.array(z.string()).default([])}`). `platform.mdx` populated: canonical sentence ported from `new-design/extracted/src/pages/bridge.html` ("Verifiable Credentials don't require a rewrite. Artagon's OID4VP→OIDC bridge…"); 3 approved variants for use on home/use-cases per the lint-bridge allow-list contract. Other pages leave `bridge` unset. lint-bridge.mjs (Phase 5.x) will enforce single-source on `/platform` and forbid verbatim repetition elsewhere.
- [x] 4.4 Author `src/content/taglines.json` with `tagline.short` (≤ 60 chars) and `tagline.triad` (3 clauses). → ✅ shipped by Copilot in commit `306913c` alongside `lint-taglines.mjs`. Spec-checked: `short` is 28 chars ("Verified, Private, Attested."); `triad` has exactly 3 clauses ("Every claim, proven." / "Every token, bound." / "Every decision, traceable."). Also includes `positioning`, `full`, `abbr`, `inline` variants for legitimate consumers (footer tagline, hero, meta description). All consumed via `import taglines from '../content/taglines.json'`; lint-taglines (3.10) enforces single-source.
- [x] 4.5 Sample `src/content/pages/writing/welcome.mdx` (non-draft) to exercise the writing detail route. → ✅ shipped at `src/content/writing/welcome.mdx` (relocated from `pages/writing/` — see 4.6 note for rationale). Content adapted from `new-design/extracted/src/pages/post-trusted-identity.html` (h1 + lede + 3-section body — Why now / What Artagon builds / What's next). Frontmatter satisfies the writing schema: `published: 2026-05-06`, `draft: false`, `tags: [announcement, identity, vc, oidc]`.
- [x] 4.6 Wire `/writing`, `/writing/[slug]`, `/writing/feed.xml` (`@astrojs/rss`). → ✅ three routes shipped: `src/pages/writing/index.astro` (post list, sorted desc by `published`, drafts filtered, empty state hides the list), `src/pages/writing/[slug].astro` (post detail with `getStaticPaths`, hero from frontmatter, body via `<Content/>`, optional `updated` marker), `src/pages/writing/feed.xml.ts` (RSS via `@astrojs/rss@4.0.18` with title/description/link/pubDate per item, `<language>en-us</language>` customData, drafts filtered). **Important deviation from spec literal**: the spec calls for posts under `src/content/pages/writing/`, but Astro 6's content config file is `src/content.config.ts` (not `src/content/config.ts` as in earlier Astro versions) and the content-layer's `glob` loader cannot scope a sub-collection to a subdirectory of another collection's base when both bases overlap. The pragmatic resolution: collection root moved to `src/content/writing/`; the spec's intent (separating writing from marketing pages, single-source frontmatter contract) is preserved verbatim. Build emits 18 routes; RSS contains 1 `<item>` (the welcome post); index lists 1 post linked to `/writing/welcome/`.

    - **Note on 4c868dc / 1381edb commit messages:** both message bodies contain the line "lint:tokens accepts oklch() without flagging it as a raw color literal" — this claim is **factually wrong**. `scripts/lint-tokens.mjs` line 56 forbids oklch outside the `public/assets/theme.css` + `DESIGN.md` allowlist; the gate only "passed" during those commits because `git ls-files` excluded the still-untracked `TrustChainIsland.css`. Once committed (1381edb) the gate would have hard-failed any subsequent `npm run build`, and was caught + corrected in 47f9898 / d489ded. History is immutable; this note is the canonical disclaimer.
  - [x] 5.1d-idle Trust-chain auto-progression. SSR keeps the fully-resolved state (step = STAGES.length) so pre-hydration HTML reads correctly for crawlers + Playwright; on hydration a `useEffect` resets `step` to 0 and walks it forward via `setTimeout` chain (400 ms kickoff, 1100 ms first-stage, 900 ms per-stage; halts on first `fail`). `is-evaluating` stages get `chain-pulse` on the number circle + `chain-spinner` next to "checking…" status. `is-pending` (not yet reached) stages mute to `--fg-3`. Skipped under `prefers-reduced-motion: reduce` AND under `navigator.webdriver` (Playwright deterministic E2E) — the chain renders fully resolved with no timer in those contexts. First-mount only — subsequent scenario changes settle immediately. DESIGN.md §6.5 "Animation primitives" + "Auto-progression timing" updated in lock-step.

Two distinct fixes in one iter: (1) **pt122 introduced a regression**: my `.hero h1` fallback rule (theme.css:657) hardcoded `letter-spacing: -0.035em` and `font-weight: 400`, which has specificity (0,1,1) and beat the `.display` utility's (0,1,0) `var(--display-tracking, …)` / `var(--display-weight, 400)` token cascade — pinning grotesk's tracking value across all hero-fonts. pt123 stripped both hardcodes from the fallback (kept canonical size + line-height + family which ARE static across variants); the .display utility now wins the cascade as designed. (2) **3 stale canonical-typography test gates** that pinned `font-weight: "500"` against a BaseLayout that has been defaulting to `data-hero-font="fraunces"` (--display-weight: 400) since commit `cfc35f4`. pt123 updated all three (`.blog-hero h1`, `home hero h1.display`, `/faq h1.display`) to honor the cascade — the `.blog-hero h1` test now asserts `weight === --display-weight` (or 500 fallback if undefined); the .display tests assert `["400", "500"].includes(weight) && weight !== "700"`. The contract is the var() cascade itself, not a hardcoded number. Diagnostic story: pt102's letter-spacing test was failing post-pt122 with delta = 1.024 px (= 0.01em × 102.4 fontSize at the ceiling). Diagnostic instrumentation added a per-element `for (sheet of styleSheets) { for (rule of cssRules) if (el.matches(rule.selectorText)) ... }` walker that surfaced the offending rule (`.hero h1 { letter-spacing: -0.035em }`) by selector + property — a pattern worth reaching for whenever a token cascade silently fails. Sweep found 2 .astro buttons without explicit type: `FaqSearch.astro` clear-search button + `ThemePreviewPanel.astro` theme button. The 7 React `.tsx` buttons (BridgeFlow, UseCases, Pillars, TweaksPanel ×2, TrustChainIsland ×2) all already carry `type="button"`. Both .astro buttons now do too. Why this matters: a `<button>` inside a `<form>` defaults to `type="submit"`, so future authoring that wraps a button in a form silently changes its behavior to "submit and reload the page". The contract closes that latent regression class. At runtime this produced nested `<main>` elements — invalid HTML AND a duplicate landmark. Fixed by either dropping the page-level wrapper (when its only attribute was a redundant id) or converting to `<div class="...">` (when the class was load-bearing for scoped CSS). Pages affected: 404, roadmap, bridge, platform, docs, search, use-cases, get-started, writing/index, writing/[slug], standards. Smoke-tested by injecting a `<main>` into a temp page → gate failed clean with `drop the page-level <main>; BaseLayout already wraps <slot /> in <main id="main-content">` + file:line. **Final cumulative:** ~134 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 274/274 (was 272) · 16 permanent regression gates · build 23 routes clean. **Iter 141 follow-on:** `pt139` `<section>` accessible-name audit. Per ARIA 1.2 spec, a `<section>` with NO accessible name has implicit role "generic" (just a styled div); WITH a name, it gets role "region" — a real WCAG landmark. The codebase already had the pattern established (HomeExplore/RoadmapTimeline/StandardsWall/PillarsIsland/.cta-section/.writing-hero/.blog-hero all use `aria-labelledby`); pt139 closed the gap on 6 top-level page sections that were missing it: home `.hero` → labelled by `hero-h1`; home `.writing-strip` + `.onramp` → labelled by NEW `id`s on their h2s (`writing-strip-h`, `onramp-h`); /faq `.faq-hero` → NEW id `faq-hero-h`; /docs `.docs-hero` → NEW id `docs-hero-h`; /console `.console-hero` → NEW id `console-hero-h`. **JSX-syntax landmine caught mid-iter**: tried initially to add `{/* */}` JSX block-comments above the writing-strip + onramp sections, but those sit inside `latestPosts.length > 0 && (...)` and `onRamp && (...)` ternary expressions. JSX/Astro requires expressions to evaluate to a single element, so adding the comment as a sibling of `<section>` made the parsed tree have two siblings → build failed with `Expected ")" but found "$$render"`. Fixed by switching to TS-style `// comment` (which isn't a JSX child). Pattern documented for future authors. **Final cumulative:** ~135 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 274/274 · 16 permanent regression gates · build 23 routes clean. **Iter 142 follow-on:** `pt140` continues pt139's `<section>` accessible-name audit by closing 4 more holdouts. Real fixes: (a) `ShimPage.astro` — ships /how /security /privacy /play /developers (5 routes); section now `aria-labelledby="shim-page-h"` pointing at the h1 (NEW id). (c) /search `<section id="results">` got `aria-label="Search results"` PLUS `aria-live="polite"` so DocSearch result-list updates announce to AT. (d) `ui/SectionHeader.astro` (the generic /vision-page section component) — added `aria-label={title}` derived from the required prop; the `{...rest}` spread still allows consumer-passed `aria-labelledby` to take precedence. The post-body / post-footer sub-sections inside `<article class="post">` were intentionally left unlabeled — `<article>` is the landmark; sub-sections within an article are typically structural, not landmarks. **Final cumulative:** ~136 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 274/274 · 16 permanent regression gates · build 23 routes clean. **Iter 143 follow-on:** `pt141` ARIA tab-pattern audit completion. The trust-chain scenario picker shipped a HALF-BUILT tabpanel pattern: each scenario dot was `role="tab"` with `aria-controls="trust-chain-decision"`, but the decision card itself had NO role — AT announced it as a generic div, breaking the AT user's "select scenario → focus jumps to its panel" mental model. pt141 added: (a) `id={`scenario-tab-${s.id}`}` on each scenario tab so the panel can aria-labelledby it dynamically, (b) `role="tabpanel"` + `aria-labelledby={`scenario-tab-${scenario.id}`}` (active scenario) on the decision card. Switched to semantic `<em class="serif">the team</em>`: `<em>` is italic by default AND carries the emphasis semantics that "the team" needs (canonical Hero.jsx pattern uses `<em class="serif">` elsewhere). JSX `style={{...}}` is intentionally OUT of scope (CSS-in-JS bypasses CSP unsafe-inline; separate discipline question). Why this matters: closes the CSP-posture regression class (postbuild SRI/CSP pass currently runs without `unsafe-inline`; new inline styles silently chip away at that) AND keeps the design-system contract centralized in component-scoped `<style>` + theme.css token chains. **Final cumulative:** ~138 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 276/276 (was 274) · 17 permanent regression gates · build 23 routes clean. **Iter 145 follow-on:** `pt143` page <title> format audit (DESIGN.md §9.5: `{Page Title} — Artagon`). The generated `.build/dist/sitemap-0.xml` shipped 22 entries including all 10 noindex routes. Sitemap presence signals "crawl me"; meta robots="noindex" signals "don't index" — Google explicitly flags the mixed signal as a soft-404 / wasted-crawl-budget regression class. Fix: extended the `@astrojs/sitemap` `filter` callback in `astro.config.ts` to exclude the 10 NOINDEX*ROUTES (404, search, privacy, how, security, status, docs, play, console, developers). Smoke-tested by temporarily disabling the astro.config.ts filter + rebuilding → gate caught **9 sitemap-noindex contradictions** (every shim/dev page that pt145 had already noindexed). Gate skips gracefully if the sitemap hasn't been built yet (CI runs build before vitest, so the path is always exercised in pipeline). **Final cumulative:** ~142 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 280/280 (was 278) · 19 permanent regression gates · build 23 routes clean. **Iter 149 follow-on:** `pt147` **caught a catastrophic SEO drift**: 12 production pages were shipping `<link rel="canonical" href="https://artagon.com/">` (pointing at the home page!) because they didn't pass `path` to `<Base>` — the SeoTags.astro `path` default is `'/'`, so every page that forgot the prop told Google "this page is a duplicate of the home page". Affected: 404, /, privacy, how, security, faq, vision, status, docs, search, play, console, developers (13 routes total — pt147 also added explicit `path="/"` on the home itself for gate-friendliness). Pre-pt148 SeoTags.astro had two templates (`og:image:alt` and `twitter:image:alt`) that unconditionally appended ` — Artagon` to the page title. Every page passes a title ending with " — Artagon" per DESIGN.md §9.5, so the rendered alts read as **"Platform — Artagon — Artagon"** / "FAQ — Artagon — Artagon" etc. — accidental brand-doubling visible in social-preview unfurlers, SEO crawlers, and screen-reader announcements of og:image. Pre-pt149 SeoTags appended ` — {76-char motto}` to every page description that didn't already contain "Verified, Private, Attested". Pre-pt144 page descriptions were 13-95 char stubs, so the append landed at ~89-171 chars — workable. After pt144 brought every description up to 150-180 chars, the append pushed every rendered meta-description to 184-245 chars — well past Google's ~155-160 SERP truncation cutoff, making the appended motto invisible on every search result. pt149 added a third condition to the append guard: skip if `description.length >= 90` (leaves room for the 76-char motto + ~5-char joiner to land at ≤166 total). Drive-by trimmed 3 pages still over budget post-guard (privacy 172→151, play 171→163, get-started 191→164). Final state: 21/21 routes have rendered meta-descriptions in 79-164 char range, with 14/21 in the canonical 100-165 sweet spot. The lesson: SEO drifts compound — pt144 was correct in isolation but broke the SeoTags append-budget invariant that pre-pt144 short stubs preserved. **Final cumulative:** ~145 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 283/283 · 21 permanent regression gates · build 23 routes clean. **Iter 152 follow-on:** `pt150` caught the THIRD form of the noindex-vs-crawler-signal contradiction (after pt146 sitemap + pt147 canonical). Pre-pt150 every noindex page (the 10 routes 404/search/privacy/how/security/status/docs/play/console/developers) shipped a `BreadcrumbList` JSON-LD block — schema.org rich-snippet that tells crawlers "this URL exists as a navigable destination at position N in a hierarchy". Combined with `noindex` it's the same mixed-signal class pt146 caught: Google parses the JSON-LD, imagines the breadcrumb, may still surface it in some rich-result contexts. /404 in particular shipped "Home → 404" — telling crawlers the error page is a child of home in the navigational hierarchy. Fix: extended SeoTags.astro `breadcrumbLd` emission with `!isNoindex` guard. Now BreadcrumbList ships only for indexable inner routes (faq, platform, roadmap, standards, use-cases, vision, writing/[slug], get-started, bridge — 9 routes). NEW `tests/lint-noindex-no-breadcrumb.test.mts` (1 vitest case, 22nd permanent regression gate) — walks built HTML, asserts no page declaring `robots=noindex` also emits `"@type": "BreadcrumbList"`. Smoke-tested by reverting the guard → caught **10 contradictions** (every noindex page). Pattern lesson: each crawler-facing signal (sitemap presence, canonical URL, BreadcrumbList JSON-LD) must independently respect noindex; pt146 + pt147 + pt150 together close all three layers. **Final cumulative:** ~146 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 284/284 (was 283) · 22 permanent regression gates · build 23 routes clean. **Iter 153 follow-on:** `pt151` Article JSON-LD author audit. Pre-pt151 every post on `/writing/[slug]` shipped `"author": {"@type": "Organization", "name": "Artagon"}` while the visible byline rendered "Giedrius Trumpickas" — visible byline / structured-data inconsistency. Root cause: /writing/[slug].astro resolved `authorName` via the authors-collection lookup but never piped it to `<Base>`; SeoTags fell back to the brand default. Fix: (a) `<Base author={authorName}>` in /writing/[slug].astro; (b) SeoTags emits author as `Person` when name !== 'Artagon', else falls back to `Organization` (which always coexists with `publisher: Organization Artagon`). This (a) inconsistent with the canonical / og:url / BreadcrumbList items in the same document, (b) makes Google's site-search rich result follow an unnecessary 301 hop on every query (since Astro 301-redirects /search/ → /search at runtime), (c) a code smell for any future contributor adding new SearchAction variants. Pre-pt153 the BreadcrumbList items in JSON-LD title-cased the URL slug for every segment. Worked for static routes (/platform → "Platform") but broke for any route whose title doesn't match the slug — every blog post: `/writing/welcome` shipped "Welcome" while the actual post title was "Trusted identity for machines and humans"; `/writing/bridge-strategy` shipped "Bridge Strategy" vs actual "Adopting verifiable credentials without rewriting your app"; `/writing/compounding-trust-chain` was close but still title-cased ("Compounding Trust Chain" vs actual "The Compounding Trust Chain"); `/vision` shipped "Vision" vs actual "Artagon Identity Platform: Vision and Roadmap". For Google's BreadcrumbList rich-result and AT structured-data preview tools, these mismatches read as inconsistent (the visible page shows X but the breadcrumb says Y). Fix: derive the LAST breadcrumb segment's `name` from the page's actual title (with the `" — Artagon"` suffix stripped); intermediate segments still use slug-titlecasing because SeoTags can't statically know intermediate-segment titles. The two structured-data namespaces were inconsistent. Fix: SeoTags now emits `<meta property="article:author" content={author}>` when type='article' AND author is present. The component shipped two pre-canonical defaults: `pinnedColor='#0EA5E9'` (legacy sky-blue from before the cyan/teal canonical) and `themeColor='#0B1220'` (legacy neutral-dark from before the OKLCH `--bg` token migration). BaseLayout already passes explicit overrides (`#3ceedd` / `#0a0d12`, the canonical sRGB equivalents from pt107), so production output was already correct — but any future consumer importing SeoIcons without props would silently ship the wrong colors. (a) `public/_redirects` destinations had trailing slashes inconsistent with `trailingSlash: "never"` in astro.config.ts: `/faqs → /faq/`, `/blog → /writing/`, `/blog/ → /writing/`. Each created a TWO-HOP redirect chain (legacy URL → trailing-slash URL → canonical no-trailing-slash URL), wasting crawl budget AND adding user-perceptible latency on cold-cache requests. (b) Both `public/security.txt` AND `public/.well-known/security.txt` had `Policy: https://www.artagon.com/security` — the wrong canonical origin (the site uses `artagon.com` no-www per CNAME + `Astro.site`). Facebook's open-graph crawler ranks pages that declare image MIME slightly higher (and OG spec recommends it for non-default formats). Pre-pt158 every page shipped `og:image` + `og:image:width|height|alt` but no `og:image:type` — incomplete OG image metadata. Fix: derived MIME from file extension via a pure switch (png/jpeg/webp/avif/svg/gif → corresponding MIME; default png because every current OG image is PNG). Now every page ships `og:image:type=image/png` (matches the actual `og-image.png` file). Future post-cover images in webp/jpeg get the correct MIME automatically. No regression gate added — the contract is "the meta tag exists with the file's correct MIME"; testing it would require parsing the actual OG image file's magic bytes, which is over-engineering for a small ranking signal. **Final cumulative:** ~154 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 287/287 · 25 permanent regression gates · build 22 routes clean. **Iter 161 follow-on:** `pt159` removed orphan `public/assets/og-image.png` + fixed `site.webmanifest.screenshots[0].src`. Pre-pt160 `public/favicon.ico` AND `public/apple-touch-icon.png` were 0-byte placeholder files at /public/ root — Astro's static-host pipeline shipped them to /dist verbatim, so legacy auto-probing browsers + bots (which probe `/favicon.ico` and `/apple-touch-icon.png` regardless of explicit `<link>` tags) got 0 bytes back, rendering as broken-icon UI in some browsers AND triggering soft-404 / "broken asset" flags in some scanners. SeoIcons provides explicit `<link rel="icon" href="/icons/favicon.ico">` and `<link rel="apple-touch-icon" href="/icons/apple-touch-icon.png">` for modern browsers, but those don't suppress the legacy auto-probe behavior — the empty root files were always served first to any client that probed before parsing HTML. Fix: copied the canonical icon binaries from `public/icons/{favicon.ico,apple-touch-icon.png}` to the root paths, so both auto-probe AND HTML-link paths now return the same canonical content (MD5-verified identical). Defense in depth across the icon-discovery layers: HTML `<link>`, /favicon.ico auto-probe, /apple-touch-icon.png auto-probe, /icons/\* explicit paths, manifest.icons[]. **Final cumulative:** ~156 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 287/287 · 25 permanent regression gates · build 22 routes clean. **Iter 163 follow-on:** `pt161` `<link rel="apple-touch-icon" sizes="...">` mismatches. Browsers + iOS scale the image when the declared size differs from actual AND log console warnings. The two misdeclared entries were also redundant with the canonical 180×180 primary apple-touch-icon (modern iOS scales 180→152/167 cleanly). Audited every named or default import across `scripts/**/*.{mjs,mts,js,ts}` (18 files). Found 2 truly orphan imports: `scripts/clean.mjs::statSync` (left over after a refactor removed the only `statSync(...)` call) and `scripts/lint-tokens.mjs::relative` (destructured from `node:path` but the body uses `dirname` / `join` / `resolve` only). The project does NOT run TypeScript or ESLint over `scripts/` (they ship as raw `node` invocations from `npm run` / postbuild / CI workflows), so the language-server `noUnusedLocals` rule does not catch this drift class. Same orphan-cleanup class as pt167 (slate CSS), pt163-pt168 (dead schema fields), pt169 (`--muted`), pt170 (`--fs-small` / `--fs-micro` / `--space-8/10/12`), pt182 (orphan SVG), pt183 (orphan npm scripts). Removed both unused imports and locked the contract with a 41st permanent regression gate `tests/lint-orphan-script-imports.test.mts`. The gate parses every named-import (`import { a, b as c, type d } from "..."`) and default-import (`import Name from "..."`) statement, asserts each locally-bound identifier (handling `as` aliases — bound name is RHS) appears in the file body outside the import statement. Side-effect-only imports (`import "./foo.mjs"`) are tolerated because they have no binding to check. Smoke-tested by injecting `statSync` and `lstatSync` into `scripts/clean.mjs` import and confirming the gate names both regressions with two actionable fix hints (wire / remove). 41st permanent regression gate.  (dd) `pt186` orphan test-imports gate + pt185 hardening. Sibling of pt185 scoped to `tests/**/*.{spec,test}.{mts,mjs,ts,js}` (80 test files). Found 1 truly orphan import: `tests/styling-a11y.spec.ts:1` imported `type Page` from `@playwright/test` but the file never used the `Page` type — leftover from an earlier helper signature. The project's vitest tsconfig is loose (no `noUnusedLocals`); Playwright bundles run via Astro's tsc with relaxed checks. The gate closes the gap. While building it, also discovered a comment-stripping bug in pt185's gate design: the naive `body.replace(/\/\*[\s\S]*?\*\//g, "")` block-comment stripper EATS embedded JS regex literals (e.g. `body.replace(/\/\*…\*\//g, …)` in `tests/lint-sitemap-noindex.test.mts:86` looked like a block comment to a string-level stripper, causing 4 false-positive orphans). Switched both pt185 and pt186 gates to anchor imports at start-of-line via `^\s*import\b` + `m` flag — imports always start at column-0 in valid JS, while JSDoc-comment example snippets sit inside `* ` or backtick prefixes, so the anchor naturally excludes them without eating regex literals. Same orphan-cleanup class as pt185 (script imports), pt182 (orphan SVG), pt167 (slate CSS), pt163-pt168 (dead schema fields). Removed `type Page` from the styling-a11y spec import and locked the contract with a 42nd permanent regression gate `tests/lint-orphan-test-imports.test.mts`. Smoke-tested by re-injecting `type Page` and confirming the gate names the regression with two actionable fix hints (wire / remove). 42nd permanent regression gate. The footnote's two claims were both drift: (1) no PGP key exists on disk; (2) the disclosure policy actually lives at `/security` (Astro page) — `.well-known/security.txt` is just the discovery endpoint that routes there via its `Policy:` field. Tolerance design: numeric majors (`22`, `"22"`, `"22.12"`) MUST match `.nvmrc` major; string LTS markers (`"lts/_"`) are allowed (explicit opt-in to LTS-floating, used by `copilot-setup-steps.yml`). Specific minor pins are tolerated as long as the major matches. (nn)`pt196` `tsconfig.json` `paths`alias consumer-presence gate. Found`tsconfig.json`declaring`paths: { "~/_": ["src/_"] }`(paired with`baseUrl: "."`) but `rtk rg 'from\s+[\"\']~/' src/ tests/`returned ZERO matches. The`~/_`alias was dead config — likely a leftover from a different project template / scaffolder. The cost is real: every TS / Astro / Vitest tooling pass forks the module resolver into a non-standard search path on every resolution attempt. Same orphan-cleanup class as pt163 (heroFont schema field — declared but no implementation), pt167 (slate CSS — defined but no`[data-theme="slate"]`consumer), pt168 (READING_WPM constant — exported but no caller), pt182 (orphan SVG), pt183 (orphan npm scripts), pt185 (orphan script imports), pt192 (ink skill). Locked the contract with a 51st permanent regression gate`tests/lint-tsconfig-paths-consumers.test.mts`. Two-mode design: (a) if `tsconfig.json`declares`paths`aliases, every alias key (modulo trailing`/_`) MUST have at least one consumer in `src/`/`tests/`/`scripts/`matching`from "<prefix>/..."`/`import("<prefix>/...")`/`require("<prefix>/...")`patterns; (b) if`paths`is empty / absent, the gate passes vacuously (post-pt196 baseline). The gate handles JSONC by stripping`// comments`and`/_ block comments _/`before`JSON.parse`. (qq)`pt199`Footer license claim vs README + disk sync gate. Found direct contradiction:`Footer.astro:115`shipped "Built on Astro · Open-source core · Apache 2.0" on every public route, while`README.md:763`§License says "Private repository - All rights reserved." and NO LICENSE file exists at the repo root. Same project, opposite claims, both shipped to public users. The legally accurate default with no LICENSE file IS "all rights reserved" per US copyright law — so the README is correct and the Footer's "Apache 2.0" claim was aspirational. Same documentation-vs-implementation drift class as pt179 (Phase-6 test claimed to drive but didn't), pt183 (verify:design-md-telemetry claimed CI-wired but wasn't), pt188 (glossary.md slate after pt167 removal), pt195 (LHCI URLs benchmarking non-canonical forms). Different surface (legal positioning vs feature wiring) but same shape: one source of truth contradicts another. Until/unless the project owner decides to ship as Apache 2.0 (which requires authoring a LICENSE file at repo root + updating README + updating package.json`license`), the Footer no longer makes a specific license assertion. Locked the contract with a 54th permanent regression gate `tests/lint-license-claim-consistency.test.mts`. Two-mode design: (a) if Footer claims a SPDX-style license name (Apache 2.0 / MIT / GPL / BSD), README §License first line MUST cite the same name AND a LICENSE / LICENSE.md / LICENSE.txt file MUST exist at repo root; (b) if Footer says "All rights reserved", README MUST NOT cite a specific SPDX license (re-introducing the contradiction). Smoke-tested by re-injecting "Apache 2.0" into the Footer and confirming the gate names BOTH the README mismatch AND the missing LICENSE file separately with two actionable fix hints (drop Footer claim / author LICENSE + update README + package.json). 54th permanent regression gate. (bbb) `pt210`extend pt199 license-claim gate to also cover`package.json.license`. After pt199 aligned the Footer ("All rights reserved") with README's authoritative claim, the third surface — `package.json`— still had NO`license`field. Per SPDX convention, code that's proprietary / no-license should declare`"license": "UNLICENSED"`. The absence triggered npm tooling warnings AND made the public legal claim inconsistent across the 3 surfaces (Footer + README say "All rights reserved"; package.json silent → unknown to license-checker tools). Same documentation-vs-implementation drift class as pt199 (Footer vs README contradiction). Different surface (npm package metadata vs HTML / markdown user-facing copy) but same shape: legal claim must be consistent across every surface that ships it. Added `"license": "UNLICENSED"`to`package.json`between`version`and`engines`. Extended pt199's regression gate (`tests/lint-license-claim-consistency.test.mts`) with a new third assertion block: (a) if Footer claims a specific SPDX license, package.json MUST declare the matching SPDX identifier (whitespace-insensitive, dash-tolerant comparison: "Apache 2.0" matches "Apache-2.0"); (b) if Footer / README cite "All rights reserved", package.json MUST declare `"license": "UNLICENSED"`(the SPDX identifier for proprietary code with no license). The gate's failure-mode hint includes the exact SPDX-form transform`Apache 2.0 → Apache-2.0`so contributors can copy-paste the fix. Smoke-tested 2 patterns: (1) deleting`license`field → caught with "undefined (expected UNLICENSED)" error; (2) declaring`"MIT"`(wrong license) → caught with the same error showing both the wrong value and expected value. No new gate file — extended the existing pt199 gate. The 4-surface license consistency (Footer + README + LICENSE-file-presence + package.json.license) is now locked end-to-end. (ccccc) `pt315` `DESIGN.md:1241` §9.2 Required-behavior-at-each-breakpoint — Explore-grid breakpoint cell drift. The table cell for "Explore grid" at the "< 720px" column read just `1-up`, but the actual HomeExplore.astro CSS (lines 147-169) declares `.home-explore__grid--primary` as 4-up by default, transitions to `repeat(2, 1fr)` at `@media (max-width: 1024px)`, and finally to `1fr` (1-up) at `@media (max-width: 540px)`. Mapping to viewport widths: ≥ 1025px is 4-up, 541-1024px is 2-up, ≤ 540px is 1-up. So at viewport widths between 541 and 720 (which falls under the table's "< 720px" column), the grid is actually 2-up — not 1-up as the table claims. Same drift class as pt216/pt261/pt310 (FILE:LINE / count anchor that fell out of sync with disk after a rebreak) but in a different shape — table cell describing visual behavior at a viewport range that doesn't align with the global breakpoints declared elsewhere in the same DESIGN.md (`--bp-sm: 480, --bp-md: 720, --bp-lg: 1024`). The Explore grid uses an INTERNAL breakpoint (540px) that doesn't align with the global `--bp-sm` (480) or `--bp-md` (720) — a deliberate per-component decision per the "Container-query boundaries inside primitives… are internal and deliberately don't match the global breakpoints" note at DESIGN.md:1230-1232. Fix: changed the cell to `2-up (collapses to 1-up at < 540px)` so the entire `< 720px` column communicates both the dominant 2-up state AND the internal-breakpoint-driven 1-up tail. Pre-pt307 §6.6 had a similar but DIFFERENT drift ("collapses to 2-up < 720 px and 1-up < 480 px") — pt307's prose rewrite already removed those wrong numbers; this iter sweeps the table sibling that was the second surface for the same fact. (mmmmmm) `pt351` `public/assets/theme.css:627`comment string`\`--token:\``—`check-design-drift.mjs`regex false-positive surface. The`pt76`archaeology comment described the linter as "flags raw colors outside`--token:`declarations" — but the script's regex`parseCssCustomProperties`at`scripts/check-design-drift.mjs:158` (`(?<![\w-])--([a-zA-Z][\\w-]*)\\s*:\\s*[^;]+;`) doesn't strip comments before matching. The comment text contained a literal `--token:`followed by a multi-line stretch ending at the first`;`in the next CSS rule. The regex matched, capturing`token`as a phantom CSS custom property —`node scripts/check-design-drift.mjs`reported "1 CSS custom property...do not resolve to a DESIGN.md frontmatter token". The script-fix would be to strip`/_ ... _/`comment blocks before the regex match. The doc-fix (this iter) rephrases the comment so`--token:`doesn't appear:`\`--token:\` declarations`→`CSS custom-property (\`--_:\`) declarations`. The `\`--_:\``form uses a wildcard`_`that doesn't match the regex's`[a-zA-Z][\\w-]_`pattern, so no false-positive. Smoke-tested`node scripts/check-design-drift.mjs`post-edit: "✓ design drift OK: 104 CSS custom properties resolved (frontmatter + allow-list); 0 orphans" — phantom`--token`finding eliminated. Drift class: comment-as-code regex collision (rare/novel — first instance this round). Different surface from the recurring drift classes (FILE:LINE-anchor-decay / phantom-change / etc.); same root cause as pt258 (source-comment archive paths) — ad-hoc regex parsers over un-stripped comments. Future-proofing observation:`parseCssCustomProperties`should strip`/\_ ... \*/`blocks before matching; out of doc-fix scope. Counters: 214+ surfaces · 65 permanent regression gates · 9 of 9 live specs validated · vitest count holds. - [x] 0.7 Adopt the conversion guidance prompt at `docs/guides/new-design-conversion.md` (v3.2, post-3-round adversarial review by Claude/Codex/Gemini). → ✅ doc shipped at `docs/guides/new-design-conversion.md` (391 lines). Note: section v3.2's React-island guidance was further updated in commit `290f111` (during PR #39) to permit React islands, since `@astrojs/react@5.0.4` was installed for the Tweaks panel — the React-NOT-installed clause below is **superseded by current state** but kept as historical context. The current React-island posture is documented in the conversion guide itself. Mandates from v3.2:
  - **Skill mandate**: load `tdd`, `typed-service-contracts`, `agent-dx-cli-scale`, and `design-md` skills from `.agents/skills/` before any conversion edit.
  - **CSP runtime blocker**: new-design HTML mocks load `unpkg.com` React/Babel CDN (e.g. `new-design/extracted/src/pages/index.html` lines 429-431) and Google Fonts CDN. Live CSP at `scripts/csp.mjs:23` is `script-src 'self'` + hashes only. Any conversion that copies mock script tags verbatim breaks runtime even if build passes. Self-host fonts under `public/assets/fonts/` per Phase 2.3 BEFORE running first page conversion.
  - **React-island guidance**: `@astrojs/react` is NOT YET installed. React islands are PERMITTED — and expected for forward-looking interactive surfaces (`/play` playground, `/console` admin, `/search` typeahead, hero trust-chain animation, Bridge SVG carousel). For each island, document the cost (bundle bytes, CSP/SRI hash regen, dep additions: `@astrojs/react` + `react` + `react-dom` + `@types/react` + `@types/react-dom`) in the conversion commit. Prefer cheaper alternatives (CSS-only `:checked`/`:has()`/`<details>`/`popover` API, vanilla `<script>` blocks, or web components like `src/scripts/tweaks.ts`) when they suffice. Marketing routes (`/`, `/platform`, `/vision`, `/roadmap`, etc.) STAY static — only interactive surfaces hydrate. Self-host all WOFF2 fonts under `public/assets/fonts/` to keep CSP `font-src 'self'` (no Google Fonts CDN).
  - **Full absorption**: USMR replaces the live marketing surface with the new-design content. Every page in `src/pages/` corresponds 1:1 with a conversion target; once USMR archives, `new-design/extracted/` becomes a historical reference and may be removed in a follow-up `cleanup-new-design-extracted` change. There is no dual-tree state — either content lives in `src/` or it does not exist on the live site.
  - **Token rename contract**: before merging `new-design/extracted/src/styles/tokens.css`, sed-rename ALL its tokens to `--nd-*` prefix (`--bg` → `--nd-bg`, `--accent` → `--nd-accent`, etc.). Append the renamed block to `public/assets/theme.css` under `/* ===== NEW-DESIGN TOKENS (OKLCH) ===== */`. Per-converted-page, alias old tokens via `:root[data-theme="midnight"] { --bg: var(--nd-bg); }` ONLY after visual verification. Never merge new-design tokens directly into a plain `:root {}` block — it would shadow the three live theme packs (`midnight`/`twilight`/`slate`).
  - **Route map authority**: live routes are NESTED at `src/pages/<route>/index.astro` (14 of 16); only `index.astro` and `404.astro` are flat. Conversion replaces page CONTENT but MUST preserve the route paths. New-design's HTML mocks have non-overlapping routes (`bridge`, `blog`, `brand-icons`, `use-cases`, `standards`, `post-*.html`) — do NOT create new routes outside the 16 live routes + 4 USMR-added routes (`/use-cases`, `/standards`, `/writing/[slug]`, `/writing/feed.xml`). Discard `bridge.html` (merged into `/platform#bridge`), `blog.html` (superseded by `/writing/[slug]`), `brand-icons.html` (defer to `add-brand-assets-and-writing-pipeline`).
  - **BaseLayout preserve contract**: lines 16-37 of `src/layouts/BaseLayout.astro` are the pre-paint theme-persistence script — DO NOT touch (theme flash if removed). All 4 slots (`head`, `header`, default body, `footer`) must remain.
  - **Hook-location reference**: the v3.2 prompt has a per-component table at `new-design/extracted/src/components/*.jsx` of every `useState`/`useEffect`/`setInterval` line and the recommended Astro alternative. Use it verbatim during conversion.

## Phase 2 — Design-system foundations (style-system)

- [~] 2.1 Add raw OKLCH palette + semantic aliases + token categories (motion, elevation, focus-ring, z-index, spacing, radius) to `public/assets/theme.css` behind cascade layers `@layer reset, tokens, utilities, components, overrides`. (NEW tokens are layered; ~150 legacy `:root` declarations remain unlayered to preserve cascade priority per "Existing Token Preservation". Spec language `"All token definitions MUST live in tokens layer"` will be reconciled by stub change `openspec/changes/migrate-legacy-tokens-to-layer/` (filed; authoring deferred until USMR archives).)
- [~] 2.2 Define `twilight` (modified — extends existing requirement) and `midnight` (new) under `[data-theme="..."]`. (Theme blocks defined; theme-aware fallbacks via `--brand-teal-rgb` per-theme. Axe-core verification deferred — `@axe-core/playwright` not yet installed; lands with the broader Playwright/axe install in Phase 6 quality gates.)

- [x] 4.1 Extend Zod schemas in `src/content.config.ts` for `pages`, `pages/writing`, and `authors` collections (eyebrow, headline, lede, CTAs[], heroFont?, accent?, tags[]). → ✅ `src/content.config.ts` updated (Astro 6 path — the Phase 4.1 commit mistakenly created `src/content/config.ts` which Astro silently ignored; corrected in Phase 4.6 commit `cd005b4`). `pages` schema requires `title`, `description`, `eyebrow`, `headline`, `lede`, `ctas[]` per spec site-content §"Type-Safe Content Schemas"; accepts optional `heroFont` (`space-grotesk` / `fraunces` / `inter-tight`), `accent`, `tags[]`. `writing` sub-collection extends `pages` with required `published` (z.coerce.date) and accepts optional `updated`, `cover`, `repo` (z.url), `author`, `draft` (default false). `authors` collection requires `name`, `slug`; accepts optional `bio`, `avatar`, `links[]` (each `{label,href}` with z.url). `cta` shape: `{label, href, rel?, variant?}` where variant ∈ `primary|secondary|ghost`. Build passes Zod validation; `pages/writing/` and `authors/` collections inert until populated in Phase 4.2 / 4.5.

The pragmatic resolution: collection root moved to `src/content/writing/`; the spec's intent (separating writing from marketing pages, single-source frontmatter contract) is preserved verbatim. Build emits 18 routes; RSS contains 1 `<item>` (the welcome post); index lists 1 post linked to `/writing/welcome/`.

    - **Note on 4c868dc / 1381edb commit messages:** both message bodies contain the line "lint:tokens accepts oklch() without flagging it as a raw color literal" — this claim is **factually wrong**. `scripts/lint-tokens.mjs` line 56 forbids oklch outside the `public/assets/theme.css` + `DESIGN.md` allowlist; the gate only "passed" during those commits because `git ls-files` excluded the still-untracked `TrustChainIsland.css`. Once committed (1381edb) the gate would have hard-failed any subsequent `npm run build`, and was caught + corrected in 47f9898 / d489ded. History is immutable; this note is the canonical disclaimer.
  - [x] 5.1d-idle Trust-chain auto-progression. SSR keeps the fully-resolved state (step = STAGES.length) so pre-hydration HTML reads correctly for crawlers + Playwright; on hydration a `useEffect` resets `step` to 0 and walks it forward via `setTimeout` chain (400 ms kickoff, 1100 ms first-stage, 900 ms per-stage; halts on first `fail`). `is-evaluating` stages get `chain-pulse` on the number circle + `chain-spinner` next to "checking…" status. `is-pending` (not yet reached) stages mute to `--fg-3`. Skipped under `prefers-reduced-motion: reduce` AND under `navigator.webdriver` (Playwright deterministic E2E) — the chain renders fully resolved with no timer in those contexts. First-mount only — subsequent scenario changes settle immediately. DESIGN.md §6.5 "Animation primitives" + "Auto-progression timing" updated in lock-step.

    Critical:
    - [ ] 5.1p.1 Fix `aria-required-children` on the trust-chain `<ol>` (`src/components/TrustChainIsland.tsx:104`). Promoting each `<li>` to `role="button"` strips its implicit `listitem` role, so the parent `<ol role="list">` reports zero `listitem` descendants — AT users hear "list with 0 items" instead of the 5-stage chain. Drop the explicit `role="list"` on the `<ol>` (browser implicit role suffices) AND restructure each stage so `role="button"` lives on an inner `<button>` or `<div>` wrapper, leaving the `<li>` as a real listitem. Re-run `tests/home-axe.spec.ts` (chromium / webkit / Mobile Safari) and confirm zero `aria-required-children` violations.

    - [ ] 5.1p.8 Token-tuning to clear 9 WCAG 1.4.3 contrast failures surfaced by axe (`color-contrast`, impact: serious). Two clusters: `--nd-fg-3` (oklch 0.45 0.008 85) on `--bg` measures 2.56:1 (consumers: `.footer-meta`, `.footer-stack`, `.footer-version`, `.hero__affiliations-label`); `--nd-fg-2` (oklch 0.62 0.008 85) on `--bg-2` measures 4.33:1 (consumers: 5 `.trust-chain__stage-sub` rows). Fix via `--nd-fg-3` → `oklch(0.62 0.008 85)` (matches current `--nd-fg-2`) and `--nd-fg-2` → `oklch(0.70 0.008 85)`, OR restrict each token's allowed consumers to bold/≥18 px contexts (per WCAG 1.4.3 large-text rule). Per ARIA 1.2 spec, a `<section>` with NO accessible name has implicit role "generic" (just a styled div); WITH a name, it gets role "region" — a real WCAG landmark. The codebase already had the pattern established (HomeExplore/RoadmapTimeline/StandardsWall/PillarsIsland/.cta-section/.writing-hero/.blog-hero all use `aria-labelledby`); pt139 closed the gap on 6 top-level page sections that were missing it: home `.hero` → labelled by `hero-h1`; home `.writing-strip` + `.onramp` → labelled by NEW `id`s on their h2s (`writing-strip-h`, `onramp-h`); /faq `.faq-hero` → NEW id `faq-hero-h`; /docs `.docs-hero` → NEW id `docs-hero-h`; /console `.console-hero` → NEW id `console-hero-h`. **JSX-syntax landmine caught mid-iter**: tried initially to add `{/* */}` JSX block-comments above the writing-strip + onramp sections, but those sit inside `latestPosts.length > 0 && (...)` and `onRamp && (...)` ternary expressions. JSX/Astro requires expressions to evaluate to a single element, so adding the comment as a sibling of `<section>` made the parsed tree have two siblings → build failed with `Expected ")" but found "$$render"`. Fixed by switching to TS-style `// comment` (which isn't a JSX child). Pattern documented for future authors. **Final cumulative:** ~135 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 274/274 · 16 permanent regression gates · build 23 routes clean. **Iter 142 follow-on:** `pt140` continues pt139's `<section>` accessible-name audit by closing 4 more holdouts. (c) /search `<section id="results">` got `aria-label="Search results"` PLUS `aria-live="polite"` so DocSearch result-list updates announce to AT. (d) `ui/SectionHeader.astro` (the generic /vision-page section component) — added `aria-label={title}` derived from the required prop; the `{...rest}` spread still allows consumer-passed `aria-labelledby` to take precedence. The post-body / post-footer sub-sections inside `<article class="post">` were intentionally left unlabeled — `<article>` is the landmark; sub-sections within an article are typically structural, not landmarks. **Final cumulative:** ~136 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 274/274 · 16 permanent regression gates · build 23 routes clean. **Iter 143 follow-on:** `pt141` ARIA tab-pattern audit completion. The trust-chain scenario picker shipped a HALF-BUILT tabpanel pattern: each scenario dot was `role="tab"` with `aria-controls="trust-chain-decision"`, but the decision card itself had NO role — AT announced it as a generic div, breaking the AT user's "select scenario → focus jumps to its panel" mental model. pt141 added: (a) `id={`scenario-tab-${s.id}`}` on each scenario tab so the panel can aria-labelledby it dynamically, (b) `role="tabpanel"` + `aria-labelledby={`scenario-tab-${scenario.id}`}` (active scenario) on the decision card. Other tab patterns audited and verified complete: PillarsIsland (tab + tablist + tabpanel + aria-labelledby per panel), UseCasesIsland (same), TrustChainIsland stage rows (separate pattern: aria-pressed buttons, not tabs). The tab-pattern contract is now consistent across all 3 island components. **Final cumulative:** ~137 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 274/274 · 16 permanent regression gates · build 23 routes clean. **Iter 144 follow-on:** `pt142` no-inline-style audit. The codebase had ONE inline `style="font-style: italic;"` on the home page writing-strip — `<span class="serif" style="font-style: italic;">the team</span>`. Switched to semantic `<em class="serif">the team</em>`: `<em>` is italic by default AND carries the emphasis semantics that "the team" needs (canonical Hero.jsx pattern uses `<em class="serif">` elsewhere). The `<span>` route was a pre-canonical artifact. NEW `tests/lint-no-inline-style.test.mts` (2 vitest cases, 17th permanent regression gate) — multi-comment-aware scanner walks every `style="..."` attribute on .astro/.tsx files. Allow-list: `display: none` / `display:none` (semicolon + whitespace normalized) for JS-toggled visibility (FAQ clear button etc.); per-line `<!-- lint-no-inline-style: ok -->` for deliberate exceptions. JSX `style={{...}}` is intentionally OUT of scope (CSS-in-JS bypasses CSP unsafe-inline; separate discipline question). Smoke-test: injected `<div style="color: red">` → gate failed clean with `style="color: red" (move to scoped <style> or use semantic HTML)` + file:line. Why this matters: closes the CSP-posture regression class (postbuild SRI/CSP pass currently runs without `unsafe-inline`; new inline styles silently chip away at that) AND keeps the design-system contract centralized in component-scoped `<style>` + theme.css token chains. **Final cumulative:** ~138 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 276/276 (was 274) · 17 permanent regression gates · build 23 routes clean. **Iter 145 follow-on:** `pt143` page <title> format audit (DESIGN.md §9.5: `{Page Title} — Artagon`). Caught 3 holdouts: `/docs` "Artagon Docs" → "Docs — Artagon"; `/console` "Artagon Console" → "Console — Artagon"; `/404` "404 — Page not found" → "Page not found — Artagon" (drop redundant "404" prefix; the page's h1 already announces the error class). NEW `tests/lint-page-title-format.test.mts` (2 vitest cases, 18th permanent regression gate). The first heuristic was too loose — caught ShimPage's `title="Privacy"` / etc. as h1-text props, not page <Base> titles. Tightened by walking backwards from each `title=` line up to the nearest `<X` element opener (max 8 lines back) and only flagging if the element is `<Base`. The fix demonstrates a useful pattern for any "is this attribute on element X?" question in JSX/Astro source. Allow-list: `Artagon — {tagline}` (home brand-first form per §9.5 carve-out); per-line `<!-- lint-page-title-format: ok -->`. Smoke-tested twice (initial loose heuristic caught real titles + ShimPage h1 props; tightened heuristic catches only real Base-title regressions). Dynamic `title={…}` (e.g. /writing/[slug], /vision) intentionally OUT of scope — those resolve to content frontmatter at build time. **Final cumulative:** ~139 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 278/278 (was 276) · 18 permanent regression gates · build 23 routes clean. **Iter 146 follow-on:** `pt144` page meta-description audit per DESIGN.md §9.5 (target 150-160 chars). Caught 8 holdouts shipping 13-79 char stubs: 6 shim-page Base meta-descriptions ("Privacy (shim)", "How it works (shim)", "Security (shim)", "Status (shim)", "Interactive OAuth/GNAP/VC playground (shim)", "Developers hub (shim)") all extended to 150-180 char informative descriptions naming the protocol stack + design-partner-program timeline; /search 46 chars → 160 (DocSearch, identity-protocol corpus); /404 70 chars → 165 (lists 4 alt destinations). Two pages were missing the noindex header: /404 (error responses shouldn't be indexed — soft-404 + thin-content penalties otherwise compound, and the alt-route list below the h1 already gets normal sitemap discovery without `nofollow`-blocking link equity); /search (search-result pages are user-facing, not crawler-facing; deep-linked /search?q=foo would otherwise become unique-URL duplicate-content footprints). Both now ship `robots="noindex, nofollow"`. The other already-noindexed routes (/privacy /how /security /status /docs /play /console /developers — 8 shim/dev pages) continue as-is. **Final cumulative:** ~141 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 278/278 · 18 permanent regression gates · build 23 routes clean. **Iter 148 follow-on:** `pt146` caught a real sitemap-vs-robots contradiction. The generated `.build/dist/sitemap-0.xml` shipped 22 entries including all 10 noindex routes. Sitemap presence signals "crawl me"; meta robots="noindex" signals "don't index" — Google explicitly flags the mixed signal as a soft-404 / wasted-crawl-budget regression class. Fix: extended the `@astrojs/sitemap` `filter` callback in `astro.config.ts` to exclude the 10 NOINDEX*ROUTES (404, search, privacy, how, security, status, docs, play, console, developers). Sitemap shrank from 22 → 13 entries (only the 13 indexable routes). NEW `tests/lint-sitemap-noindex.test.mts` (2 vitest cases, 19th permanent regression gate) — walks every src/pages/\*.astro, parses each file's `<Base robots="...">` attribute (comment-stripped), and asserts pages declaring `noindex` do NOT appear in the built sitemap. Maps src paths to URLs (`src/pages/privacy/index.astro` → `/privacy` → `https://artagon.com/privacy`). Smoke-tested by temporarily disabling the astro.config.ts filter + rebuilding → gate caught **9 sitemap-noindex contradictions** (every shim/dev page that pt145 had already noindexed). Gate skips gracefully if the sitemap hasn't been built yet (CI runs build before vitest, so the path is always exercised in pipeline). **Final cumulative:** ~142 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 280/280 (was 278) · 19 permanent regression gates · build 23 routes clean. **Iter 149 follow-on:** `pt147` **caught a catastrophic SEO drift**: 12 production pages were shipping `<link rel="canonical" href="https://artagon.com/">` (pointing at the home page!) because they didn't pass `path` to `<Base>` — the SeoTags.astro `path` default is `'/'`, so every page that forgot the prop told Google "this page is a duplicate of the home page". Affected: 404, /, privacy, how, security, faq, vision, status, docs, search, play, console, developers (13 routes total — pt147 also added explicit `path="/"` on the home itself for gate-friendliness). Fix: each page now passes `path="/<route>"` to `<Base>`. Verified at build time — every route's canonical now matches its actual URL. NEW `tests/lint-canonical-url.test.mts` (2 vitest cases, 20th permanent regression gate) — comment-aware multi-line scanner walks every `<Base>` opening tag in src/pages/**/\*.astro (skipping dynamic [slug] routes which compute path at render time) and asserts each carries `path=`. Smoke-tested by injecting a `<Base>` without `path` → gate failed clean with `<Base> missing path= prop`. **The single biggest SEO regression caught in the entire pt121→pt147 sweep — every shim/error/dev page was being announced as duplicate-of-home content for an unknown but long period of time.\*\* **Final cumulative:** ~143 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 282/282 (was 280) · 20 permanent regression gates · build 23 routes clean. **Iter 150 follow-on:** `pt148` no-double-brand audit. Pre-pt148 SeoTags.astro had two templates (`og:image:alt` and `twitter:image:alt`) that unconditionally appended ` — Artagon` to the page title. Every page passes a title ending with " — Artagon" per DESIGN.md §9.5, so the rendered alts read as **"Platform — Artagon — Artagon"** / "FAQ — Artagon — Artagon" etc. — accidental brand-doubling visible in social-preview unfurlers, SEO crawlers, and screen-reader announcements of og:image. The home page (brand-first " Artagon — {tagline}" form per the §9.5 carve-out) rendered as "Artagon — Trusted Identity for Machines and Humans — Artagon". Fix: a single `ogImageAlt` const that strips the redundant suffix when the title already mentions Artagon (suffix OR prefix). Both meta tags now consume it. NEW `tests/lint-og-double-brand.test.mts` (1 vitest case, 21st permanent regression gate) — walks every built `.html` in `.build/dist/**` and asserts no `Artagon — Artagon` em-dashed double-brand anywhere. Smoke-tested by reverting one of the two fixes → gate failed across multiple routes (the gate scans built HTML, so it catches BOTH og:image:alt AND twitter:image:alt regressions, AND any future template that develops the same bug). The "scan built HTML" pattern caught the pt148 fix incompleteness on the FIRST run — would have shipped silently with og:image:alt fixed but twitter:image:alt still broken. **Final cumulative:** ~144 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 283/283 (was 282) · 21 permanent regression gates · build 23 routes clean. **Iter 151 follow-on:** `pt149` caught a **compounding-drift** introduced by pt144. Pre-pt149 SeoTags appended ` — {76-char motto}` to every page description that didn't already contain "Verified, Private, Attested". Pre-pt144 page descriptions were 13-95 char stubs, so the append landed at ~89-171 chars — workable. After pt144 brought every description up to 150-180 chars, the append pushed every rendered meta-description to 184-245 chars — well past Google's ~155-160 SERP truncation cutoff, making the appended motto invisible on every search result. pt149 added a third condition to the append guard: skip if `description.length >= 90` (leaves room for the 76-char motto + ~5-char joiner to land at ≤166 total). Drive-by trimmed 3 pages still over budget post-guard (privacy 172→151, play 171→163, get-started 191→164). Final state: 21/21 routes have rendered meta-descriptions in 79-164 char range, with 14/21 in the canonical 100-165 sweet spot. The lesson: SEO drifts compound — pt144 was correct in isolation but broke the SeoTags append-budget invariant that pre-pt144 short stubs preserved. **Final cumulative:** ~145 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 283/283 · 21 permanent regression gates · build 23 routes clean. **Iter 152 follow-on:** `pt150` caught the THIRD form of the noindex-vs-crawler-signal contradiction (after pt146 sitemap + pt147 canonical). Pre-pt150 every noindex page (the 10 routes 404/search/privacy/how/security/status/docs/play/console/developers) shipped a `BreadcrumbList` JSON-LD block — schema.org rich-snippet that tells crawlers "this URL exists as a navigable destination at position N in a hierarchy". Combined with `noindex` it's the same mixed-signal class pt146 caught: Google parses the JSON-LD, imagines the breadcrumb, may still surface it in some rich-result contexts. /404 in particular shipped "Home → 404" — telling crawlers the error page is a child of home in the navigational hierarchy. Fix: extended SeoTags.astro `breadcrumbLd` emission with `!isNoindex` guard. Now BreadcrumbList ships only for indexable inner routes (faq, platform, roadmap, standards, use-cases, vision, writing/[slug], get-started, bridge — 9 routes). NEW `tests/lint-noindex-no-breadcrumb.test.mts` (1 vitest case, 22nd permanent regression gate) — walks built HTML, asserts no page declaring `robots=noindex` also emits `"@type": "BreadcrumbList"`. Smoke-tested by reverting the guard → caught **10 contradictions** (every noindex page). Pattern lesson: each crawler-facing signal (sitemap presence, canonical URL, BreadcrumbList JSON-LD) must independently respect noindex; pt146 + pt147 + pt150 together close all three layers. **Final cumulative:** ~146 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 284/284 (was 283) · 22 permanent regression gates · build 23 routes clean. **Iter 153 follow-on:** `pt151` Article JSON-LD author audit. Pre-pt151 every post on `/writing/[slug]` shipped `"author": {"@type": "Organization", "name": "Artagon"}` while the visible byline rendered "Giedrius Trumpickas" — visible byline / structured-data inconsistency. Root cause: /writing/[slug].astro resolved `authorName` via the authors-collection lookup but never piped it to `<Base>`; SeoTags fell back to the brand default. Fix: (a) `<Base author={authorName}>` in /writing/[slug].astro; (b) SeoTags emits author as `Person` when name !== 'Artagon', else falls back to `Organization` (which always coexists with `publisher: Organization Artagon`). Pattern: structured-data-vs-rendered-content consistency is its own contract class — SEO-pipeline bugs are invisible to humans during dev but corrupt every external surface (rich results, author-attribution UI, AT structured-data preview). **Final cumulative:** ~147 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 285/285 (was 284) · 23 permanent regression gates · build 23 routes clean. **Iter 154 follow-on:** `pt152` JSON-LD URL trailing-slash consistency. astro.config.ts sets `trailingSlash: "never"`, so every internal URL across the site is in the no-trailing-slash form. But the WebSite SearchAction `urlTemplate` shipped `https://artagon.com/search/?q={search_term_string}` — trailing slash before the query string. This (a) inconsistent with the canonical / og:url / BreadcrumbList items in the same document, (b) makes Google's site-search rich result follow an unnecessary 301 hop on every query (since Astro 301-redirects /search/ → /search at runtime), (c) a code smell for any future contributor adding new SearchAction variants. Fix: dropped the `/` before `?q=`. Pattern: trailingSlash inconsistency between Astro config + JSON-LD templates is invisible at runtime (the redirect just works) but corrupts crawler signals. **Final cumulative:** ~148 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 286/286 (was 285) · 24 permanent regression gates · build 23 routes clean. **Iter 155 follow-on:** `pt153` BreadcrumbList leaf-name accuracy. Pre-pt153 the BreadcrumbList items in JSON-LD title-cased the URL slug for every segment. Worked for static routes (/platform → "Platform") but broke for any route whose title doesn't match the slug — every blog post: `/writing/welcome` shipped "Welcome" while the actual post title was "Trusted identity for machines and humans"; `/writing/bridge-strategy` shipped "Bridge Strategy" vs actual "Adopting verifiable credentials without rewriting your app"; `/writing/compounding-trust-chain` was close but still title-cased ("Compounding Trust Chain" vs actual "The Compounding Trust Chain"); `/vision` shipped "Vision" vs actual "Artagon Identity Platform: Vision and Roadmap". For Google's BreadcrumbList rich-result and AT structured-data preview tools, these mismatches read as inconsistent (the visible page shows X but the breadcrumb says Y). Fix: derive the LAST breadcrumb segment's `name` from the page's actual title (with the `" — Artagon"` suffix stripped); intermediate segments still use slug-titlecasing because SeoTags can't statically know intermediate-segment titles. Verified across 7 routes: leaf names now match the rendered <title> minus the brand suffix. The two structured-data namespaces were inconsistent. Fix: SeoTags now emits `<meta property="article:author" content={author}>` when type='article' AND author is present. Both defaults updated to canonical: pinnedColor → `#3ceedd` (sRGB of OKLCH `--accent`); themeColor → `#0a0d12` (sRGB of `[data-theme="dark"] --bg = oklch(0.14 0.008 260)`). Two PWA manifest files shipped: `site.webmanifest` (canonical, 11 icons, complete metadata, theme `#0a0d12`) AND `manifest.webmanifest` (legacy stub, 2 icons with stale paths `/assets/icon-192.png` instead of canonical `/icons/icon-192.png`, theme `#0B1220` legacy color, missing `start_url`/`scope`/etc.). The HTML references only `/site.webmanifest` via SeoIcons.astro:69; `manifest.webmanifest` had ZERO references anywhere in the codebase. But everything in `/public` ships to `/dist` verbatim, so the orphan was deployed alongside the canonical. PWA installers / Lighthouse / some crawlers probe both filenames — a stale orphan is a false-positive trap (the legacy theme color `#0B1220` would surface in audits as "manifest theme matches OS" failing, when the actual canonical `site.webmanifest` was correct). Deleted. (a) `public/_redirects` destinations had trailing slashes inconsistent with `trailingSlash: "never"` in astro.config.ts: `/faqs → /faq/`, `/blog → /writing/`, `/blog/ → /writing/`. Each created a TWO-HOP redirect chain (legacy URL → trailing-slash URL → canonical no-trailing-slash URL), wasting crawl budget AND adding user-perceptible latency on cold-cache requests. Fixed: destinations now match `trailingSlash: "never"` directly. (b) Both `public/security.txt` AND `public/.well-known/security.txt` had `Policy: https://www.artagon.com/security` — the wrong canonical origin (the site uses `artagon.com` no-www per CNAME + `Astro.site`).
