Facebook's open-graph crawler ranks pages that declare image MIME slightly higher (and OG spec recommends it for non-default formats). Pre-pt158 every page shipped `og:image` + `og:image:width|height|alt` but no `og:image:type` — incomplete OG image metadata. Fix: derived MIME from file extension via a pure switch (png/jpeg/webp/avif/svg/gif → corresponding MIME; default png because every current OG image is PNG). Now every page ships `og:image:type=image/png` (matches the actual `og-image.png` file). Future post-cover images in webp/jpeg get the correct MIME automatically. No regression gate added — the contract is "the meta tag exists with the file's correct MIME"; testing it would require parsing the actual OG image file's magic bytes, which is over-engineering for a small ranking signal. **Final cumulative:** ~154 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 287/287 · 25 permanent regression gates · build 22 routes clean. **Iter 161 follow-on:** `pt159` removed orphan `public/assets/og-image.png` + fixed `site.webmanifest.screenshots[0].src`. Two og-image files existed: `public/assets/logos/og-image.png` (canonical, used by `og:image` meta + pt148/pt158 image-alt + image-type) and `public/assets/og-image.png` (legacy, MD5 `3a3e13b3...` ≠ canonical `bd5b6514...`). After pt156 deleted manifest.webmanifest, the site.webmanifest's `screenshots[0].src` was the only remaining reference to the legacy path. PWA installers (Lighthouse / Microsoft Edge "Install as app" / Android Chrome's "Add to Home Screen") consume manifest.screenshots; social unfurlers consume og:image. The two surfaces showed DIFFERENT images for the same site — visually inconsistent across consumer classes. Fix: pointed `site.webmanifest.screenshots[0].src` at canonical `/assets/logos/og-image.png`; deleted the orphan legacy file. Now both surfaces show the same canonical OG image. **Final cumulative:** ~155 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 287/287 · 25 permanent regression gates · build 22 routes clean. **Iter 162 follow-on:** `pt160` 0-byte favicon orphans replaced with real canonical icon copies. Pre-pt160 `public/favicon.ico` AND `public/apple-touch-icon.png` were 0-byte placeholder files at /public/ root — Astro's static-host pipeline shipped them to /dist verbatim, so legacy auto-probing browsers + bots (which probe `/favicon.ico` and `/apple-touch-icon.png` regardless of explicit `<link>` tags) got 0 bytes back, rendering as broken-icon UI in some browsers AND triggering soft-404 / "broken asset" flags in some scanners. SeoIcons provides explicit `<link rel="icon" href="/icons/favicon.ico">` and `<link rel="apple-touch-icon" href="/icons/apple-touch-icon.png">` for modern browsers, but those don't suppress the legacy auto-probe behavior — the empty root files were always served first to any client that probed before parsing HTML. Fix: copied the canonical icon binaries from `public/icons/{favicon.ico,apple-touch-icon.png}` to the root paths, so both auto-probe AND HTML-link paths now return the same canonical content (MD5-verified identical). Defense in depth across the icon-discovery layers: HTML `<link>`, /favicon.ico auto-probe, /apple-touch-icon.png auto-probe, /icons/\* explicit paths, manifest.icons[]. **Final cumulative:** ~156 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 287/287 · 25 permanent regression gates · build 22 routes clean. **Iter 163 follow-on:** `pt161` `<link rel="apple-touch-icon" sizes="...">` mismatches. SeoIcons.astro had 3 apple-touch-icon link tags; 2 of them declared `sizes` that didn't match the referenced file's actual PNG dimensions: `sizes="152x152" href="/icons/icon-128.png"` (file is 128×128) and `sizes="167x167" href="/icons/icon-180.png"` (file is 180×180). Browsers + iOS scale the image when the declared size differs from actual AND log console warnings. The two misdeclared entries were also redundant with the canonical 180×180 primary apple-touch-icon (modern iOS scales 180→152/167 cleanly). Fix: dropped both misdeclared entries; kept the canonical 180×180 primary. NEW `tests/lint-icon-sizes-match.test.mts` (1 vitest case, 26th permanent regression gate) — walks every `<link rel="icon"|"apple-touch-icon" sizes="WxH" href="...">` in built `.build/dist/index.html`, reads the referenced PNG's IHDR chunk (offset 16, big-endian uint32 width+height — no third-party image lib), and asserts WxH matches actual dimensions. Smoke-test: re-added the 167×167 misdeclaration → gate caught with `declared sizes="167x167" but file ... is 180x180`. The IHDR-parsing approach is generalizable: any future icon-pipeline regression (a contributor swapping in the wrong file) trips immediately. **Final cumulative:** ~157 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 288/288 (was 287) · 26 permanent regression gates · build 22 routes clean. **Iter 164 follow-on:** `pt162` aligned author-collection filename with declared slug. The `src/content.config.ts` `authors` schema documents `slug` as "URL slug — kebab-case, matches filename". But the file at `src/content/authors/writing-blog.mdx` declared `slug: "trumpyla"` — a contract violation. Astro 6's `glob` content loader derives each entry's `id` from filename relative to `base` (default behavior). So id="writing-blog", but post `author: "trumpyla"` lookup did `authorByName.get("trumpyla")` — should have failed. The byline rendered correctly anyway (verified pt151), suggesting either an Astro 6 nuance with slug-as-id OR a fortuitous match somewhere. Either way: the filename-vs-slug drift was a latent bug class waiting for any future Astro version that strictly enforces id=filename. Fix: renamed `writing-blog.mdx` → `trumpyla.mdx`. Required cache invalidation (`.astro/` + `.build/cache/`) because Astro's content layer caches filename-to-id mappings — pt162 required `rm -rf .astro` before the rebuild succeeded; future contributors hitting a similar rename should know this. Verified post-rename: byline still renders "Giedrius Trumpickas", Article JSON-LD still ships `Person: Giedrius Trumpickas`, article:author OG tag still emits — pt151+pt154 contract holds. **Final cumulative:** ~158 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 288/288 · 26 permanent regression gates · build 22 routes clean. **Iter 165 follow-on:** `pt163` removed dead `heroFont` content frontmatter. The schema in `src/content.config.ts` defined `heroFont: z.enum(["space-grotesk", "fraunces", "inter-tight"]).optional()` — but the runtime canonical set per `[data-hero-font]` in theme.css is `["grotesk", "fraunces", "dmserif", "mono"]`. So **the schema's enum tokens didn't match the runtime tokens**: `space-grotesk` and `inter-tight` are pure schema fictions. AND no page actually read `post.data.heroFont` to propagate it onto `<html data-hero-font>` — every page rendered BaseLayout's hardcoded `data-hero-font="fraunces"` default. So the entire heroFont frontmatter system was: (a) dead (never read), (b) broken-by-name (schema enum ≠ runtime tokens). Pre-pt163 6 .mdx files declared `heroFont:` (5× `space-grotesk`, 1× `fraunces`) — all silently ignored at render. Fix: removed `heroFont` from all 6 .mdx files + dropped the schema field. Comment in content.config.ts explains the removal + what's needed if per-page hero-font is re-introduced (both schema enum AND BaseLayout wire-up land together). Discovered separately during the audit: this user's environment has `ignore-scripts=true` in their global .npmrc, so `npm run build` skips ALL postbuild gates locally (CSP, SRI, lint:tokens, lint:skip-link, lint:taglines, lint:design, lint:design-md-uniqueness). The build "succeeds" but ships without CSP/SRI in the local dev environment. CI/production builds (without ignore-scripts) DO run postbuild — and currently fail at `verify-font-self-hosting.mjs` because `font-src 'self'` doesn't allow Google Fonts CDN. The `self-host-woff2-fonts` OpenSpec change tracks the canonical fix. Not actionable in a single Ralph iter; documented here for context. **Final cumulative:** ~159 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 288/288 · 26 permanent regression gates · build 22 routes clean. **Iter 166 follow-on:** `pt164` continues pt163's dead-schema-field cleanup. Audited every optional field in the content schemas; found 2 more pure-dead fields (zero setters AND zero consumers): `accent` (on `pageBase` parent schema) and `repo` (on `writing` extension). Both ran `z.string().optional()`/`.url().optional()` with comments suggesting a future feature ("--accent-warm" override; "code-anchored post" repo link) that was never wired. Pre-pt164 post.data.accent and post.data.repo were pure schema fictions — TypeScript-typed but always undefined. Removed both fields with comments documenting what's needed if either is re-introduced (schema entry + page-level reader + appropriate display surface). The pt163 + pt164 pattern: when content-frontmatter schema has a field with zero setters AND zero readers, it's dead code that misleads future authors into thinking a feature exists. Verified other potentially-dead fields are alive: `updated` (1 consumer — Article modifiedTime), `cover` (1 consumer — articleImage), `draft` (4 consumers — RSS / index / sort filters). **Final cumulative:** ~160 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 288/288 · 26 permanent regression gates · build 22 routes clean. **Iter 167 follow-on:** `pt165` Tweaks pre-paint allow-list sync gate. The Tweaks state has 5 enums (accent, density, theme, hero-font, writing-widget) that are dual-sourced: `src/scripts/tweaks-state.ts` exports canonical TS constants (ACCENTS / DENSITIES / THEMES / HERO_FONTS / WRITING_WIDGETS) consumed by the React island, AND `src/components/Tweaks.astro` duplicates them as inline JS arrays in the `is:inline` pre-paint script (which can't import TS modules synchronously before React hydrates). All 5 enums are currently in sync, but the dual-sourcing creates a drift risk — adding a new value to one but not the other causes the pre-paint to silently drop new values, leaving users with a flash of default state until React hydrates. NEW `tests/lint-tweaks-allowlist-sync.test.mts` (5 vitest cases — one per enum, 27th permanent regression gate) — extracts each array literal via regex (handles the optional `: ReadonlyArray<T>` TS annotation) and asserts the inline + canonical lists are deeply equal (order-sensitive — chip-label order pre/post hydration must match). RFC 9116 §3 specifies two locations for security.txt: PRIMARY `/.well-known/security.txt` (required) + LEGACY `/security.txt` (fallback). Both must contain identical content — pt157 caught a drift where both files had `Policy: https://www.artagon.com/security` (wrong subdomain — site uses bare `artagon.com`); fixed both in the same commit. NEW `tests/lint-security-txt-sync.test.mts` (1 vitest case, 29th permanent regression gate) — asserts `public/security.txt` and `public/.well-known/security.txt` are byte-identical. Smoke-tested by appending an `Acknowledgments:` line to one copy → gate caught with deep-equal diff. Without this gate, future contributor edits to one location only would silently send mixed signals to RFC-9116-compliant scanners (which check the PRIMARY) vs legacy scanners (which check ROOT). **Final cumulative:** ~168 commits · canonical-typography 25/25 · vitest 294/294 (was 293) · 29 permanent regression gates · build 22 routes clean. **0 orphan CSS tokens.** **Iter 175 follow-on:** `pt173` aligned brand-link `aria-label` casing across Header + Footer. Audited every `.astro` template for inline event-handler attributes (`onclick="…"`, `onload="…"`, `onerror="…"`, …) — the third member of the project's "string→runtime-code" XSS-sink family alongside `set:html` and `innerHTML`. Found exactly one drift: `src/components/ThemePreviewPanel.astro:11` shipped `<button … onClick={\`\_\_setTheme('${t}')\`}>`which Astro emits verbatim as`onclick="…"` in the rendered HTML (Astro doesn't have JSX programmatic-listener semantics — it's a string attribute). The dev-only ThemePreviewPanel was the last surface in the codebase doing string-to-event-handler conversion; under the project's strict CSP (`scripts/csp.mjs`postbuild gate enforces`script-src`without`'unsafe-inline'`) it would either be silently blocked at runtime or force a CSP weakening if the panel ever escaped `import.meta.env.DEV`. Deleted `public/assets/logo-wordmark.svg` and locked the contract with a 38th permanent regression gate `tests/lint-orphan-public-svg.test.mts`. Scope deliberately narrow: SVGs only (PNG variants under `public/assets/logos/` are loaded via templated paths the gate can't reliably resolve), root-level only (subdir SVGs scoped by their own README/index). Docs (`.md`) are NOT consumers — they describe assets but don't reference them at runtime/build time. Smoke-tested by injecting `public/assets/zzz-fake-orphan.svg` and confirming the gate names the regression with two actionable fix hints (wire to consumer / delete per CLAUDE.md). 38th permanent regression gate.  (aa) `pt183` orphan npm-scripts gate + wire `verify:design-md-telemetry` into CI. Audited every script in `package.json`. Found 5 orphans (no caller in CI workflows, docs, scripts, postbuild composition, or npm lifecycle). Of these: `prepare` is auto-invoked by `npm install` (npm lifecycle hook — false positive); `test:design-prerequisites` and `test:lint-tokens` are intentional convenience aliases for ad-hoc local single-test runs (the underlying tests are enumerated by `test:node`); `verify:font-self-hosting` is the spec-cited entry point per `self-host-woff2-fonts/specs/font-self-hosting`, kept as alias even though postbuild calls the underlying script directly via raw node. The fifth — `verify:design-md-telemetry` — was real drift: defined as alias, the script existed at `scripts/verify-design-md-telemetry.mjs` (per `adopt-design-md-format` Phase 2.10 to assert lint:design makes ZERO outbound network calls via `unshare -n` Linux network-namespace isolation), but the archived `adopt-design-md-format` `tasks.md` line claimed "✅ Telemetry: verify-design-md-telemetry.mjs runs in CI" while NO CI workflow actually invoked it. Documentation-vs-implementation drift class same as pt178 (openspec spec `public/favicon.svg`), pt179 (AGENTS.md `tests/screen-reader.spec.ts` Phase-6), pt175 (AGENTS.md ast-grep table missing rows). Wired the verifier into `.github/workflows/design-md-lint.yml` after `Run design.md lint` step (Linux runner has `unshare`, the script's exit-0 path is taken; on macOS local the script exits 2 with a warning — Linux CI is the authoritative gate per the script's own design). Locked the contract with a 39th permanent regression gate `tests/lint-orphan-npm-scripts.test.mts` carrying an allow-list with per-entry rationale for the 4 intentional orphans (`test:design-prerequisites`, `test:lint-tokens`, `verify:font-self-hosting`, plus npm lifecycle hooks recognised separately). Smoke-tested by injecting `lint:totally-fake-orphan` and confirming the gate names the regression with four actionable fix hints (wire / compose / allow-list / delete). 39th permanent regression gate. Audited every named or default import across `scripts/**/*.{mjs,mts,js,ts}` (18 files). Found 2 truly orphan imports: `scripts/clean.mjs::statSync` (left over after a refactor removed the only `statSync(...)` call) and `scripts/lint-tokens.mjs::relative` (destructured from `node:path` but the body uses `dirname` / `join` / `resolve` only). The project does NOT run TypeScript or ESLint over `scripts/` (they ship as raw `node` invocations from `npm run` / postbuild / CI workflows), so the language-server `noUnusedLocals` rule does not catch this drift class. Same orphan-cleanup class as pt167 (slate CSS), pt163-pt168 (dead schema fields), pt169 (`--muted`), pt170 (`--fs-small` / `--fs-micro` / `--space-8/10/12`), pt182 (orphan SVG), pt183 (orphan npm scripts). Removed both unused imports and locked the contract with a 41st permanent regression gate `tests/lint-orphan-script-imports.test.mts`. The gate parses every named-import (`import { a, b as c, type d } from "..."`) and default-import (`import Name from "..."`) statement, asserts each locally-bound identifier (handling `as` aliases — bound name is RHS) appears in the file body outside the import statement. Side-effect-only imports (`import "./foo.mjs"`) are tolerated because they have no binding to check. Smoke-tested by injecting `statSync` and `lstatSync` into `scripts/clean.mjs` import and confirming the gate names both regressions with two actionable fix hints (wire / remove). 41st permanent regression gate.  (dd) `pt186` orphan test-imports gate + pt185 hardening. Sibling of pt185 scoped to `tests/**/*.{spec,test}.{mts,mjs,ts,js}` (80 test files). Found 1 truly orphan import: `tests/styling-a11y.spec.ts:1` imported `type Page` from `@playwright/test` but the file never used the `Page` type — leftover from an earlier helper signature. The project's vitest tsconfig is loose (no `noUnusedLocals`); Playwright bundles run via Astro's tsc with relaxed checks. The gate closes the gap. While building it, also discovered a comment-stripping bug in pt185's gate design: the naive `body.replace(/\/\*[\s\S]*?\*\//g, "")` block-comment stripper EATS embedded JS regex literals (e.g. `body.replace(/\/\*…\*\//g, …)` in `tests/lint-sitemap-noindex.test.mts:86` looked like a block comment to a string-level stripper, causing 4 false-positive orphans). Switched both pt185 and pt186 gates to anchor imports at start-of-line via `^\s*import\b` + `m` flag — imports always start at column-0 in valid JS, while JSDoc-comment example snippets sit inside `* ` or backtick prefixes, so the anchor naturally excludes them without eating regex literals. Same orphan-cleanup class as pt185 (script imports), pt182 (orphan SVG), pt167 (slate CSS), pt163-pt168 (dead schema fields). Removed `type Page` from the styling-a11y spec import and locked the contract with a 42nd permanent regression gate `tests/lint-orphan-test-imports.test.mts`. Smoke-tested by re-injecting `type Page` and confirming the gate names the regression with two actionable fix hints (wire / remove). 42nd permanent regression gate.  (ee) `pt187` ORG.contactFootnote PGP-claim drift + on-disk gate. Pivoted from doc/test imports to runtime-data drift. Found `src/data/organization.ts:29` `ORG.contactFootnote` claiming "PGP key & security disclosure policy at artagon.com/.well-known" — but `rtk rg -l 'PGP|pgp|gpg' src/ public/` shows ZERO PGP/GPG material anywhere in the codebase, and `public/.well-known/` only contains `security.txt` (RFC 9116 discovery, no key). The footnote's two claims were both drift: (1) no PGP key exists on disk; (2) the disclosure policy actually lives at `/security` (Astro page) — `.well-known/security.txt` is just the discovery endpoint that routes there via its `Policy:` field. The footnote is surfaced to users on the home on-ramp card; security researchers following the promise would 404 looking for a key. Same documentation-vs-implementation drift class as pt178 (openspec spec `public/favicon.svg`), pt179 (AGENTS.md `tests/screen-reader.spec.ts` Phase-6), pt180 (README.md `LogoVariants.astro` post-pt72-deletion), pt181 (CONTRIBUTING.md `openspec/AGENTS.md` ghost path) — but scoped to user-visible runtime data, not docs. Rewrote footnote to: "Security disclosure policy at artagon.com/security; .well-known/security.txt is the discovery endpoint." Reflects reality. Locked the contract with a 43rd permanent regression gate `tests/lint-organization-claims.test.mts`. Two assertions: (a) ORG.contactFootnote MUST NOT mention `PGP key` / `GPG key` unless `public/` or `public/.well-known/` contains a `.asc` / `.pgp` / `.gpg` file (or filename contains `pgp` / `gpg`); (b) every `.well-known/X` path mentioned in the footnote MUST resolve to an on-disk file at `public/.well-known/X`. Smoke-tested 2 regression patterns: re-injecting a PGP-key claim → caught with disk-status hint; injecting `.well-known/totally-fake.txt` → caught with named missing path. 43rd permanent regression gate. (pp)`pt198` `package.json`engines.node + sync gate. Found`package.json`had NO`engines`field at all —`.nvmrc`(informational, consumed by nvm/fnm/asdf) and the 10 CI workflows (gated by pt193) pinned Node 22, but`npm install`accepted any Node version silently. Bug surface: a contributor running unsupported Node (no`.nvmrc`-aware version manager) installs deps without warning, hits cryptic runtime errors when ESM resolution, `node:test`flags, or`fetch()`body-stream behavior diverges from the v22 surface. Same documentation-vs-implementation drift class as pt193 (CI Node version vs`.nvmrc` — release.yml pinned Node 20), pt183 (`verify:design-md-telemetry`claimed CI-wired but wasn't until pt183 fixed it). Different surface (npm engines vs CI YAML) but same shape: the version-pinning chain had a silent gap. Added`"engines": { "node": ">=22.0.0" }`to`package.json`so`npm install`enforces the floor. Locked the contract with a 53rd permanent regression gate`tests/lint-package-engines-node.test.mts`. The gate enforces: (a) `package.json`declares an`engines.node`field; (b) the lower-bound MAJOR version in the engines.node range matches`.nvmrc`'s major. Handles common semver range forms (`>=22.0.0`, `^22`, `~22.12.0`, `22`). The full version-pinning chain post-pt193 + pt198: `.nvmrc`(informational) + 10 CI workflow`node-version:`pins (gated by pt193) +`package.json`engines.node (gated here) — three sources of truth all locked to the same major via 2 cross-cutting regression gates. Smoke-tested 2 patterns: (1) deleting the`engines`field → caught with "absent" error; (2) declaring`">=20.0.0"`(wrong major) → caught with "major mismatch" error showing both sources. 53rd permanent regression gate. (qq)`pt199`Footer license claim vs README + disk sync gate. Found direct contradiction:`Footer.astro:115`shipped "Built on Astro · Open-source core · Apache 2.0" on every public route, while`README.md:763`§License says "Private repository - All rights reserved." and NO LICENSE file exists at the repo root. Same project, opposite claims, both shipped to public users. The legally accurate default with no LICENSE file IS "all rights reserved" per US copyright law — so the README is correct and the Footer's "Apache 2.0" claim was aspirational. Same documentation-vs-implementation drift class as pt179 (Phase-6 test claimed to drive but didn't), pt183 (verify:design-md-telemetry claimed CI-wired but wasn't), pt188 (glossary.md slate after pt167 removal), pt195 (LHCI URLs benchmarking non-canonical forms). Until/unless the project owner decides to ship as Apache 2.0 (which requires authoring a LICENSE file at repo root + updating README + updating package.json`license`), the Footer no longer makes a specific license assertion. Locked the contract with a 54th permanent regression gate `tests/lint-license-claim-consistency.test.mts`. Two-mode design: (a) if Footer claims a SPDX-style license name (Apache 2.0 / MIT / GPL / BSD), README §License first line MUST cite the same name AND a LICENSE / LICENSE.md / LICENSE.txt file MUST exist at repo root; (b) if Footer says "All rights reserved", README MUST NOT cite a specific SPDX license (re-introducing the contradiction). (bbb) `pt210`extend pt199 license-claim gate to also cover`package.json.license`. After pt199 aligned the Footer ("All rights reserved") with README's authoritative claim, the third surface — `package.json`— still had NO`license`field. Per SPDX convention, code that's proprietary / no-license should declare`"license": "UNLICENSED"`. The absence triggered npm tooling warnings AND made the public legal claim inconsistent across the 3 surfaces (Footer + README say "All rights reserved"; package.json silent → unknown to license-checker tools). Same documentation-vs-implementation drift class as pt199 (Footer vs README contradiction). Different surface (npm package metadata vs HTML / markdown user-facing copy) but same shape: legal claim must be consistent across every surface that ships it. Added `"license": "UNLICENSED"`to`package.json`between`version`and`engines`. Extended pt199's regression gate (`tests/lint-license-claim-consistency.test.mts`) with a new third assertion block: (a) if Footer claims a specific SPDX license, package.json MUST declare the matching SPDX identifier (whitespace-insensitive, dash-tolerant comparison: "Apache 2.0" matches "Apache-2.0"); (b) if Footer / README cite "All rights reserved", package.json MUST declare `"license": "UNLICENSED"`(the SPDX identifier for proprietary code with no license). The gate's failure-mode hint includes the exact SPDX-form transform`Apache 2.0 → Apache-2.0`so contributors can copy-paste the fix. Smoke-tested 2 patterns: (1) deleting`license`field → caught with "undefined (expected UNLICENSED)" error; (2) declaring`"MIT"`(wrong license) → caught with the same error showing both the wrong value and expected value. No new gate file — extended the existing pt199 gate. The 4-surface license consistency (Footer + README + LICENSE-file-presence + package.json.license) is now locked end-to-end. Caught and fixed a regex-design bug while building:`\bNode (\d+)\+\b`— the trailing`\b`requires`+`(non-word) to be followed by a word char, but`+`in "Node 18+ and npm" is followed by space (non-word), so`\b`fails. Fixed by dropping the trailing`\b`(the`+`itself is the natural right delimiter). Smoke-tested by injecting`Node 18+ and npm`into project.md and confirming the gate names "openspec/project.md: \"Node 18+\" cites Node 18+". The pt212 + pt213 + pt214 fix together updates every present-tense Astro/Node version claim across 6 surfaces (AGENTS.md + 2 docs + openspec/{config.yaml, project.md, contributing.md} + new-design-conversion.md), all locked to package.json + .nvmrc. Subtle case-sensitivity drift: macOS case-insensitive HFS+/APFS made`existsSync(".github/pull_request_template.md")`resolve to the uppercase file (so the pt190 path-citation gate at`tests/lint-openspec-contributing-paths.test.mts`passed locally), but case-sensitive Linux CI would NOT resolve the lowercase form. The pt190 gate uses`existsSync`which inherits the host filesystem's case sensitivity — a documented gap that the gate doesn't close. Fixed the citation to canonical uppercase`PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md`with an inline note about the case-sensitive Linux-CI requirement so future contributors don't reintroduce the lowercase form. The pt190 gate still passes (case-aligned); a future iter could extend the path-citation gate stack to use`git ls-files`instead of`existsSync`for case-sensitive validation, but that would require shelling out to git (slower) and would only catch this specific drift class. Manual triage stays the pragmatic approach. Same drift class as pt273 (non-existent file references) but specifically about case-sensitivity rather than file-existence. Why italicized prose and NOT `{/_ MDX comment _/}`or`<!-- HTML comment -->`: Prettier's markdown plugin mangles `{/\_ \*/}`into`{/\_ \_/}`(invalid MDX), and MDX 3.x rejects`<!-- -->` outright (`@mdx-js/rollup`error:`Unexpected character. To create a comment in MDX, use {/\* text \*/}`). Italicized prose round-trips cleanly through both. Added new vitest gate `tests/lint-content-pages-frozen-phase-claims.test.mts`(vitest count 339 → 340, gate count 65 → 66) that enumerates`src/content/pages/\_.mdx`, strips `{/\_ \*/}`+`<!-- -->`comments (defense-in-depth for both shapes), and forbids`(ships|will ship|will land) in Phase X.Y`and`until Phase X.Y`patterns. Live Playwright probe at 540 px viewport revealed C · split rendered 3 columns squished to ~150 px each. Diagnosis: pt109's variant override `[data-writing-widget="C · split"] .writing-strip__list { grid-template-columns: 1.5fr 1fr 1fr }` had higher specificity than the base `@media (max-width: 540px) .writing-strip__list { grid-template-columns: 1fr }` rule, so the 3-up split persisted on mobile. Fix: wrapped the variant override in `@media (min-width: 541px)` AND added a parallel `@media (max-width: 540px) [data-writing-widget="C · split"] .writing-strip__list { grid-template-columns: 1fr }` rule. Live probe verified: 540 px → 476 px single column ✓; 1422 px → 486 + 324 + 324 (1.5fr 1fr 1fr) ✓. Other variants (B · 3-up, A · strip, D · ticker) verified canonical at both viewports. `pt114` Fixed FAQ h1 rendering hero-sized (102 px) when canonical wants ~60 px FAQ-page size. Diagnosis via Playwright probe: markup was `<h1 class="gradient-text" style="font-size:clamp(2rem,1.2rem+3vw,3rem)">`. The inline `1.2rem+3vw` (no `calc()`) is **invalid CSS** — browsers ignore the entire `clamp()` and fall back to the bare h1's `var(--fs-h1)` = 102.4 px hero size. Plus `gradient-text` is a legacy class with no CSS rule defined (orphan). Fix: replaced markup with `<h1 class="faq-hero__title display">` so the canonical `.display` utility's token cascade applies (Space Grotesk Medium / `--display-tracking` / `--display-weight`). Added scoped `.faq-hero__title { font-size: clamp(40px, 5vw, 64px); line-height: 1.05 }` for FAQ-page sizing (smaller than home Hero clamp(56-108) since FAQ is a content page not the marketing front door). Live probe verified: 64 px ceiling at 1422 viewport, 500 weight, Space Grotesk family. `pt115` Two more invalid `clamp()` instances + permanent linter gate. (a) `.faq-lead { font-size: clamp(1rem, 0.65rem + 1vw, 1.15rem) }` — same broken syntax pt114 caught on the FAQ h1; the entire clamp() was unparseable so paragraph fell back to body 16 px. Plus non-canonical `color-mix(..., white 6%)` color override. Fix: added `lead` utility class to markup so `.lead { font-size: 20; color: --fg-1; line-height: 1.5 }` cascades; scoped rule retains only max-width + margin-top. (b) `.hero h1 { font-size: clamp(2rem, 2.6vw + 1rem, 4rem) }` in theme.css — same pattern. Even though `.hero h1.display` (scoped) overrode it, the broken syntax was a latent landmine. Wrapped middle in `calc()`. (c) NEW `tests/lint-clamp-syntax.test.mts` — 2 vitest cases that walk every `.css/.astro/.mdx/.tsx/.jsx` file and flag any `clamp(MIN, VAL, MAX)` where any arg has bare `+` or `-` arithmetic without `calc()`. Strips `/* */` block comments AND `//` line comments (in .astro/.tsx) to avoid prose-mention false positives. Backstops the failure mode pt114+pt115 fixed — future devs adding `clamp(2rem, 1rem + 2vw, 3rem)` (no calc) will fail the build instead of silently shipping a broken clamp that falls back to cascade defaults. **vitest 243 → 245.** `pt116` Permanent regression gates for the FAQ h1 (pt114) and 404 h1 (pt70) page-level sizing. Pre-pt116 only home Hero + /writing index had explicit canonical-typography size gates; FAQ + 404 were dependent on the global lint-clamp-syntax gate (pt115) for the same class of bug but had no per-page assertion. Two new cases assert: FAQ h1 in [40, 64] AND `< 80` (would be 102 if invalid clamp regression returns) + weight 500 (canonical .display cascade); 404 h1 in [36, 60] AND `< 80`. canonical-typography 19 → 21 cases. Loop now backstops every page-level h1 with explicit size assertion: home Hero (clamp 56-108), /writing index (clamp 44-84), /faq (clamp 40-64), /404 (clamp 36-60), /writing/[slug] post-detail (clamp 40-68). `pt117` ShimPage h1 was rendering at 102 px (hero-sized) on 5 placeholder pages (/how, /security, /privacy, /play, /developers) because the bare `<h1>` picked up `var(--fs-h1)` = `clamp(56, 7.2vw, 108)`. Same class of drift pt114 caught on FAQ (canonical doesn't run hero-sized headings on content/placeholder pages). Fix: ported ShimPage from inline `style="margin:.2rem 0"` h1 + `class="discrete"` description → `class="shim-page__title display"` h1 + `class="shim-page__lede lead"` description; added scoped CSS for canonical sizing (`clamp(40, 5vw, 64)` h1, `padding: clamp(48, 8vw, 80)` section). The .display + .lead utility cascades apply canonical font-weight (500), tracking, color (fg-1 instead of the dim fg-3 .discrete shipped). Live probe verified /how: h1 64 / fg / 500, lede 20 / fg-1 / 400. `pt118` /docs page had **TWO h1 elements** (a11y violation — only one h1 per page is canonical) AND both rendered at 102 px hero-sized (same class of drift pt114 caught on FAQ + pt117 fixed on ShimPage). The "Documentation in preparation" h1 promoted to h2 (single-h1 rule). Both headings get the .display utility for canonical 500 weight + Space Grotesk + tracking. Plus inline-style legacy padding / margin replaced with scoped CSS using canonical clamps. `.discrete` description swapped to `.lead` utility. Live probe verified: 1 h1 (64 px / 500) + 1 h2 (48 px / 500). `pt119` /console + /search h1 hero-sized regression. Same drift class as pt114/pt117/pt118 — bare `<h1>` rendered at 102 px. Ported both to `.display` utility + scoped `clamp(40, 5vw, 64)` h1 sizing. /console: `.discrete` description swapped to `.lead`. /search: inline-style margin/padding moved to scoped CSS using canonical clamps. Live probe verified /console: h1 64 px / 500. `pt120` (a) **Live UX response: "when hovering with mouse on trust chain it vibrates".** Pre-pt120 `.trust-chain__stage` used `transition: all 0.45s` which animates EVERY property change — when mouse hover triggered a border-color change during the auto-cycle's stage state transitions, both transitions competed and produced visible jitter. Restricted transition to canonical 3 properties (border-color, background, box-shadow). Layout properties now snap immediately. (b) NEW canonical-typography case: comprehensive hero-size guard walks 7 representative routes (/, /writing, /writing/welcome, /faq, /how, /docs, /console) and asserts: every page has 1 h1 (a11y baseline + max 1 per page rule); home Hero h1 ≥ 80 px (canonical hero); every other route < 80 px (content-sized). Test scoped to `main h1` to exclude Astro's dev-toolbar overlay h1s ("Audit" / "Settings"). canonical-typography 21 → 22 cases. Backstops the entire pt114/pt117/pt118/pt119 fix series — any new placeholder route added without canonical h1 sizing will fail this single gate. **Final cumulative:** 117 commits · vitest 245/245 · node:test + tweaks 39/39 · **canonical-typography 22/22** · build 23 routes clean. Loop totals after 100 iterations: ~94 fix commits · token defs 172 → 109 (-37 %) · ~1119 lines dead code removed · 5 permanent regression gates active (canonical-typography, webfonts, brace-balance, zombie-fallbacks, lint:tokens token-aware mode) · 50+ `var()` migrations across 5+ files · 2 user-facing UX bugs fixed live from screenshots (nav focus rectangle pt79; bg color pt87/pt90).

## Parallelism notes

- Phases 2 + 4 can start in parallel; Phase 5 depends on both.
- Phases 6 and 7 are independent; both consume Phase 4.
- Phase 8 consumes 3 + 5.
- Phases 9, 10, 11 are independent after Phase 3, but share `BaseLayout.astro` — stage edits.

## Rollback

Revert PRs in reverse phase order. Per-phase revert is self-contained: each phase writes to its own capability dir and its own `src/` tree. The cross-cutting files (`BaseLayout.astro`, `theme.css`, `csp.mjs`) are touched by Phases 2/3/9/10/11 — if multiple revert, restore those files to the pre-Phase-2 baseline.
